(Don't) hold me (back)

by obsesja

Summary

It was a fucking irony that Atsumu, who dreamed about being a professional athlete, turned out to be an Omega, whereas his stupid twin, who wanted to be a professional cook, turned out to be an Alpha. Somebody up there had really fucked up, in Atsumu's opinion, because if they switched, they wouldn't even be having this conversation. But no. Sport was for Alphas, the kitchen for Omegas. End of discussion.

Well, at least it shoud be, because he wasn't going to give up so easily.

Ready to fight for their dreams, the twins decide to swap places, putting at stake their lives, health and future.

Chapter 1

He had known they were in trouble the moment their parents sat them down in the living room with sour faces. But he had never expected that they would do something like that! Osamu was sitting in silence and looking at them stone-faced, clearly defeated. Atsumu wasn't going to give up so easily.

Their father, Haruo, knitted his eyebrows. "Do what?" he asked sarcastically. "Secure a good life for you, young man? Because this is exactly what we are trying to do here!"

"It's not! You are trying to ruin my life! Since I can remember, I have always wanted to play soccer professionally! I'm good enough, but the only thing you care about is what the neighbors will say!"

"I hate you!" Atsumu looked at his parents with eyes shining from tears. "You can tell us that it's for our own good, but it's really not! You're fucking egoists, and I hate you!"

With those words, he turned on his heels and ran to his room upstairs. Their father shouted after him, but he didn't stop. He slammed the door forcefully.

"Jeez, do you want to break my nose?" Osamu went in and closed the door like a civilized person. Atsumu looked at him with rage.

Every product and dish was put into a traffic lights system, marking green things that were healthy, orange that you should eat sporadically and red, a complete no-go if you wanted to live past your thirty birthday. Atsumu liked healthy food, so choosing something from green stuff was easy and quick. It took him some time to find a free table because there were thousands of students eating there, but he managed to secure a spot near one of the exits.

Wolfing down his lunch, he noticed Akaashi a few tables further, talking to Sakusa of all people. They looked comfortable. Sakusa was showing Akaashi something on his phone, and Akaashi was nodding in understanding. Were they a couple? Probably yes. To be honest, they made a good match. Both dark, tall and handsome.

He shrugged and finished his food, updating his schedule on Google Drive. His name appeared on the soccer team’s roster, so he could choose the days and time for his classes that could overlap with training. He could also switch classes if they happened during a match or other club responsibilities. Although soccer was an extracurricular activity, a lot of players got offered spots in professional teams after graduation, so many people were ready to overlook their shortcomings in academic field. Atsumu was ready to do everything in his power to be in that group of selected stars-to-be.

After his classes that day, he went straight to the locker room, humming under his nose. There were many players there, including loud Bokuto and tranquil Ushijima. Atsumu picked his locker on a whim and changed into his sport gear. They looked like a bunch of clowns, each of the rookies clad in their high school colors, not yet equipped with official jerseys.

“Miya! Hey!” Bokuto waved to him with a smile. “Are you a ninja or something? I woke up at around six and you were already gone!” 

Right. Bokuto and his stupid, mouth-watering pheromones. Atsumu winced internally. He had to do something about it.

“I went out for a walk,” he responded.

“Before six in the morning?”

Atsumu shrugged. “I always sleep poorly in new places.”

Especially without Samu , he thought.

Their coach introduced himself as Yamamoto Rei and he was a fucking sadist. He asked the first years to state their names and position, and then the whole team had to run around the pitch for one hour, and THEN he made them run suicides that he TIMED. Each player who did not meet his standards could forget about touching the ball — they were sent back to running laps till the end of the training. Atsumu was very, very happy he didn’t end up as one of them.

To be honest, they didn't do anything new or groundbreaking. The drills were well-known and practiced. The only difference was that the players around him were much better than he was used to. And he was supposed to do more in less time. He had to admit he was almost knocked out by the sheer amount of drills they had to perform. The first time in his life, he was actually glad when the practice ended. He dreamed about a shower and snuggling to his pillow under a blanket.

The locker room was a happy mess of players. Someone put the music on in the shower room, making some of the guys wiggle their asses to the beat. Atsumu would gladly shake his but, one, Osamu would never do this, and two, he was still an Omega among dozens of Alphas. There were some Betas here and there, but they were a poor line of defense in the face of those bulky and horny Alphas.

There was Komori Motoya, for example, a former Itachiyama goalkeeper, who saved many impossible balls, including Sakusa’s bended ones. Komori played with Sakusa in high school, so he knew his style and habits, but watching him dig his shots was still hella impressive.

There was also Tendou Satori. Atsumu made a mental note to keep away from this one. He was so fucking weird. He could pass the ball in the ideal moment to the striker, missing the offside so narrowly it should be prohibited. He had an astonishing sense of teamplay and timing that made dealing with him really annoying.

And the Alphas… There was Ushijima Wakatoshi — a tractor of a man if Atsumu had to be honest. Great technical skills and left-footed which gave him a big advantage over the opponents. His stamina was really impressive.

The next one worth mentioning was definitely Bokuto, with a never-ending supply of excitement and energy. Atsumu noticed Bokuto could be very immature and funny outside the pitch, but when he stepped on it he dedicated all his attention and energy to the game. He had great intuition and was this kind of person who made people feel things. He effortlessly made people drag their asses off their seats in anticipation.

Kuroo Tetsurou was a stubborn and consistent motherfucker with an infuriating smirk and lazy vibe. He slide-tackled the opponents, taking the ball cleanly, without fouls. He loved kicking the ball between people’s legs, especially Bokuto’s. It was the right man in the right place.

And, of course, Sakusa. A quiet predator. His technical skills were on par with Ushijima, strength with Bokuto, and speed with Atsumu. And those bended balls… Atsumu was dying of curiosity how he did it. What separated him from the rest was the fact he could play every position. In his heart, he was a striker through and through, but he took the time to learn ins and outs of each position, including the goal, making him an outstanding all-rounder. Atsumu wanted to test him sometime and check if he could score against him.

And he was already making plans in his head how to use all this talent to win the collegiate championship.

He snapped out of his thoughts and finished his shower, going to the locker room. Getting dressed was easier than showering. Nobody paid attention to him. Some people looked while addressing him and asking something, but it was completely normal. The captain announced that at the end of the week there would be a socializing event for the team to make them more comfortable with each other.

“Are you going back to the dorms?” Bokuto asked, following him out the lockers. He was wearing his bag like a kid, with the strap of his bag hanging around his neck. He looked like he wanted to suffocate himself.

“I’ve never run so much in my life,” Atsumu admitted. “I just wanna sleep.”

If your pheromones don’t fuck it up for me, he didn’t say aloud. He could ask him to wear patches to sleep, but how should he justify this request? What was he supposed to say? That he was gay and Bokuto’s scent made him hard? He was too pretty to get socked in the face, especially from someone as strong as Bokuto.

“The practice is brutal for people with no stamina,” Bokuto agreed, although he didn’t look like he couldn’t catch up the past few hours. He didn’t look bothered at all. He had the best time in suicides, too. “Last year, Kuroo run suicides for two weeks straight before he passed. He cried from happiness.”

“You want to tell me we are going to do this each practice?” Atsumu asked incredulously.

“Yeah, until everybody makes it. And then once a month, to see if we keep fit. The coach is all about stamina. The match takes ninety minutes so if we drop after the first half, who is going to score and defend?”

Atsumu wasn’t about to argue with that logic, but it still felt like a little much. It would take some time to get used to it.

At night he slept poorly again, and the next practise was even more exhausting than the first one. Two second longer and he would be running the whole time. The effort made him so tired he almost ran — in snail’s pace, of course — to the cafeteria for some well deserved food. He knew he couldn’t eat there too often, it was too expensive, but he decided to take full advantage of it since he still could.

“Miya-san.” Atsumu turned to the voice behind him and saw Akaashi. “Hi.”

“Hey, Akaashi. What’s up?”

“I’m fine,” the Omega replied politely. “How is the university?”

“Exhausting,” Atsumu admitted. He filled his tray and moved forward. Akaashi did the same, choosing two yoghurts, some fruit salad and a mound of curry. “The coach is obsessed with running.”

Akaashi laughed. “So I’ve heard from my friend.”

“Sakusa?” The question escaped before he could stop himself.

Akaashi looked at him with surprise. “How did you know?”

“Ah,” Atsumu smiled sheepishly. “I’ve seen you together, that’s all.”

They moved forward and went to pay.

“Mhm. Our families know each other. My dad is a medical director in one of the hospitals here, and Kiyoomi’s dad in another one. They hoped we would be together but neither of us was interested. We’re too similar.”

Atsumu paid with his cafeteria card and waited for Akaashi to pay for his meal. Then they chose a comfortable table in the corner that was secluded from the prying eyes, giving them some privacy and peace.

Akaashi turned out to be a talkative person. It surprised Atsumu because he took him for a quiet and insular person. He was anything but, you just had to talk about stuff he cared about and he gladly participated in a conversation.

“So? Why Tokyo if you are from Kobe? It’s so far away.” Akaashi remarked.

“My parents sorta made me.”

“And you listened?”

Good point, Atsumu thought. Why did you listen, Samu?

Hr shrugged.

“Well, I probably shouldn’t be surprised. A lot of people did the same. Including me.”

“You’re an Omega. You didn’t have a choice.” Akaashi raised his eyebrows, hearing his dry response. Atsumu sighed. “It happened to my brother. He got a full scholarship in some soccer academies, but our parents didn’t let him go. They forced him to take courses for Omegas in Osaka.”

“Wow, okay. Sensitive topic, I got it. So—” Akaashi smirked, “why so invested in Sakusa? Or maybe it’s me that drew your attention?”

Atsumu choked on his juice. “You can’t just notice someone familiar in the crowd randomly?”

“Alphas never ‘notice randomly.’ It means you want a petty rivalry with Kiyoomi or you are trying to hit on me.”

“You talked to me first,” Atsumu pointed out.

“You didn’t even try to protest.”

“You’re cute.” And he wasn’t joking. Akaashi was a perfect Omega. He looked good, was fashionable, intelligent and, apparently, funny. “But you’re not my type. Sorry.”

“Oh, okay.” Akaashi didn’t seem bothered. “So it's a rivalry with Kiyoomi, I get it.”

“I don’t want to compete with him. We’re on the same team.”

“That doesn’t exclude competing. I would even go and say it’s the opposite.”

“Why are we even talking about it? I’m not interested in him.” Sakusa? Really? No way in hell. “He’s a good soccer player and he bends the ball like a crazy man, but that’s all. I bet he’s a total nerd and tight-ass off the pitch.”

Those good-looking ones usually were.

Akaashi chickled. “Maybe a little,” he admitted. “Kiyoomi plays the violin.” Atsumu made a gesture with his hands, as if he wanted to say ‘I told you so’, but Akaashi wasn’t finished. “But he’s definitely not a tight-ass and I can prove it.”

“How?”

Akaashi took out his phone and scrolled for a moment. He turned the screen in Atsumu’s direction, giggling like a schoolgirl.

“Are you sure you don’t like him?” Atsumu was more than sceptical. “You behave like you do.”

“He’s my idol. You will see. This is a recording from a very important recital that took place a few months ago. His parents told him he should stop wasting his time and study medicine. Kiyoomi-kun wasn’t very happy and then he performed like this.”

Akaashi tapped the screen. Atsumu frowned and looked carefully at the scene that was being displayed. The music in the background was weird, and the grunting and snarling even weirder… The light focused on Sakusa who was standing a little to the side, playing a pretty lively piece on his violin. Atsumu had never been to that kind of event, but even he knew that Sakusa’s Converse and black jeans ripped at the knee and left thigh weren’t the anticipated outfit. He had a white shirt and dark tie, sure, but he rolled the sleeves casually and just looked very… out of place.

He was good. Well, he sounded good. He had a soundtrack, though, which was pretty fierce for classical music. Did he hear the drums? The person recording cursed in disbelief and moved the camera to the astounded audience. Sakusa wasn’t even standing in one place like it usually was, he was walking, playing the whole time, not caring about anything and anyone. He kept on rocking. The music got faster here and slower there, and Sakusa looked like he was giving a performance of his life. And he probably was.

When the music stopped and the whole recital hall was engulfed in silence, Sakusa bowed and left the scene calmly.

“I gather this wasn’t supposed to look like that?”

“I bet this recital hall had never heard the sound of drums before. The piece Kiyoomi played… It’s actually ‘Moon Trance’ by Lindsay Stirling. A very cool violinist but our elites don’t accept her because she creates more pop, rock and hip-hop music. Nobody dared to do something like this before. The whole upper crust here has been talking about this performance for months.”

Atsumu laughed. Maybe Sakusa had bigger balls than he gave him credit for.

“Fine, maybe he has it in himself. He had to be in such big trouble.”

“Oh, he was totally screwed! But his parents accepted defeat and gave him their blessing to do whatever he wanted. “Akaashi smirked. “I only mentioned he’s my idol and my parents quickly gave in and let me choose what to apply for in uni. And it goes unsaid they don’t try playing matchmaking between me and Kiyoomi anymore.”

Sakusa Kiyoomi. Who would have thought? Maybe he judged him too quickly.

The evening practice went without a hitch. Well, almost. Bokuto was hit twice in the face with the ball and almost knocked out, peculiarly distracted and down. (Kuroo was running laps for the whole practice afterwards, because he laughed so hard at his friend that he peed himself.) Atsumu had no idea what could happen and make someone so cheerful and happy so sad and dejected, but he decided to ask later.

On their way back to the dorms he tried to pry out of Bokuto what was wrong, but his roommate remained tight-lipped and only answered with the saddest pout Atsumu had seen in his entire life. Atsumu lost his patience and left him to sulk in peace.

At night he couldn’t sleep, but he wasn’t the only one. Bokuto was tossing and turning and taking way too many bathroom breaks.

“Miya? Are you asleep?”

Atsumu sighed. Bokuto was loud even when whispering. “No,” he answered, watching the ceiling. He was so tired…

“Do you and Kaashi—?” He stopped for a second. “Are you together?”

Atsumu blinked. “Me and who?”

“You and Akaashi Keiji? If yes that’s totally cool but if you break his heart I will never forgive you!” Bokuto tried to sound threateningly but it came out rather lamely. Bokuto and threats just didn’t mix. “I saw you yesterday with him in the cafeteria!”

Atsumu snorted internally. First he thought that Akaashi dated Sakusa, and now Bokuto thought he dated Akaashi. He realised how stupid this assumption was only after hearing Bokuto drew the same conclusions from the same type of situation.

“No? I met him— like, two days ago.”

Why was Bokuto even asking?

“You looked like you knew each other well!” He accused, wiggling on the bed.

“I think we’re just on the same wavelength. Akaashi isn’t my type.”

“Kaashi’s everybody’s type!” Bokuto sounded offended by Atsumu’s suggestion that somebody could not want Akaashi.

And fine, he kind of understood it. If he were an Alpha, he wouldn’t walk by indifferently. But he wasn’t. Why Bokuto…?

Oh. Oh! He dug deep in his mind, trying to connect all the dots. And Bokuto’s behavior suddenly made sense. His dejection, sadness, absent-mindedness…

Bokito had hots for Akaashi!

In a moment of pure geniusness, Atsumu sat on his bed and turned to Bokuto.

“Bokuto— I will tell you something if you promise to keep it a secret.”

Intrigued, Bokuto also sat and tilted his head like a damn owl. He nodded, impatient to be let on this ‘secret’.

“You promise?” Atsumu prompted.

“I promise! My mouth is sealed!” he assured.

Atsumu waited him out a little to make the whole ‘secret’ more dramatic. He hoped he wasn’t just commiting social suicide and Bokuto would really keep it a secret. “I’m gay,” he finally revealed. “That’s why Akaashi isn’t my type. To be honest,” he cleared his throat, “I would actually like you to wear the patches at night, because— well, your pheromones are really fucking strong and it kinda drives me crazy.”

Silence. Atsumu held his breath, anticipating Bokuto’s reaction.

“So you and Kaashi— There is nothing?” Bokuto asked after a moment with a lot more livid voice than before.

“Nothing.”

“And from the two of us you want me?”

“Ugh, want is too strong, okay?” He didn’t want to scare him off. A lot of people were intolerant assholes. There was a reason for Osamu’s sexual orientation remaining a well kept secret among twins. If their charade came out, Osamu would disembowel him for ruining his reputation. “You pheromones are just strong and I can’t sleep. It’s not like I want to fuck you or something.”

“Sure, sure! Cool! I don’t mind!” Bokuto punched the air, beaming at him like an idiot. Well, he was an idiot. “And you’re sure you’re gay?”

“I’m positive.”

“One hundred percent?”

“Enough percent to know that Akaashi is yours.”

Bokuto choked on his spit, swinging his hands in protest. Atsumu didn’t believe him for a second. Bokuto wore his heart on his sleeve and Atsumu could see right through him.

“It’s really not like that! I just—”

“Oh? So you don’t want to make a deal that in exchange for the patches, I will tell him some nice things about you?”

“Really?!” Bokuto shot from the bed with excitement. He didn’t even try to hide his happiness anymore. He jumped on Atsumu’s bed and engulfed him in a bear hug. Atsumu rounded his eyes, feeling the soul leave his body with all the strength Bokuto used on him. “You are the best! I’m putting the patches on now!”

Only Bokuto could hug a guy who just told him he was gay and felt desire towards him (although the bilogical one).

That night Atsumu couldn’t sleep again. Not because of Bokuto’s strong pheromones, but his even stronger excitement that kept both of them up till dawn.

Chapter 3

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

“So— You’re gay.”

Atsumu choked so much that the coke spurted out his nose. Coughing and wincing at the burning in his nose, he covered his face and tried to wipe the table with some napkins.

“Who the hell told you that?!” he choked out, slowly cleaning up the mess he had made. Akaashi was watching him with amusement, that asshole.

“It explains questions about Sakusa,” the dark-haired Omega added. Atsumu choked once again.

“You’re joking!”

Atsumu met Sakusa only on training and sometimes in the kitchen, but their interactions didn’t go beyond ‘hi’. Atsumu once asked him about university and soccer, but Sakusa’s reticence quickly killed their awkward interactions. Atsumu gave up on trying. Sakusa was a weirdo anyway. Atsumu had never seen someone wiping clean utensils before using them.

“Where did you hear that?” He repeated the question.

“From Kenma,” Akaashi admitted. His eyes were still shining with amusement. Before Atsumu managed to ask who the hell was Kenma, Akaashi explained, “He heard it from his childhood friend, Kuroo, who was told by Bokuto.”

Atsumu groaned internally. He was going to kill Bokuto! He told him at night and Akaashi already knew at lunch the next day?! Atsumu expected a little bit more privacy in such a huge university.

“What an asshole! He promised not to tell!”

“I think Kuroo is an exception. Bokuto-san is unable to hide anything from him.”

“Wait a second… You know Bokuto?”

Akaashi shook his head.

“He’s my senpai from Fukurodani. Our school had a very good team which made it to nationals each year, so I’ve heard a lot about him. I’ve seen him in the halls and school cafeteria, too, but never talked to him personally.”

Atsumu barely stopped himself from babbling to Akaashi that Bokuto had a crush on him.

“What do you think about him?” he asked instead. “Apart from the fact he’s such a blabbermouth.”

Akaashi winced. It wasn’t a good sign. “I don’t want to talk badly about your friends,” he said apologetically. Atsumu raised his eyebrows, prompting him to say more. Akaashi shrugged his shoulders. “He’s a pig, okay? In high school he was always flirting with Omegas and dating one after the other. He constantly informed everybody how cool he is. It was so annoying.”

RIP Bokuto.

“I’ve known him for a couple of days, so—” Atsumu shrugged as well. He decided to go back to a different problem. “Can I trust that you won’t spread the news further? About— you know? I don’t want to advertise it.”

“Of course. I can keep a secret, unlike some people. But I have no idea if Kiyoomi plays for the same team. He never said anything.”

“What—? Christ, I’m not interested in him!”

“So why are you opposing so much?”

“Maybe you secretly love Bokuto?”

“Yeah, when pigs fly!”

“Why are you opposing so much?” Atsumu threw the words right into his face.

Akaashi blinked and laughed. “Okay, I get it. I won’t say anything.”

“Good.”

On his way to afternoon classes, Atsumu called Osamu. They both updated their schedules on a shared Google Drive, so Atsumu knew his twin was free for the next hour.

Osamu only sighed when Atsumu told him what had happened since they last talked. He promised him great pain for this social suicide.

“How are classes?” Atsumu changed the topic.

“I’ve learned so much stuff already.” Osamu’s eyes brightened with excitement. He was very reserved by nature, but Atsumu knew him too well not to notice. “Some theoretical classes suck. And you have to help me pass English, our teacher is British and he can say only ‘ohayou’ and ‘arigatou’ in Japanese. Suna cried.”

“Yeah, right. I’m sure you sobbed in your sleeve, you loser. You can’t even introduce yourself properly.”

“Don’t forget who helped you with math for years, you fucking parasite!”

Atsumu stuck out his tongue at him. ‘Helped’ was definitely too much. Atsumu wasn’t a bad student. His grades were actually decent, but Maths for some reason was beyond his comprehending powers. Osamu didn’t get most of the school subjects, but Maths was easy as breathing for him, so he exchanged tasks with Atsumu and taught each other. They both loved calling the other one a loser and idiot.

“Did mum call you?” Osamu asked.

“Yeah, but I couldn’t answer, I had training. I texted her.”

Their mum tried a couple of times with text messages, asking about the university, if everything was okay, and if he made some new friends. Atsumu brushed her off with some half-assed answer that everything was fine and he was doing alright. She tried to pray more out of him, but he wasn’t interested. Till the very last day at home Atsumu was curt to his parents. When they drove him to the university in Osaka, he kind of just said ‘bye’ and went on his way before they had a chance to hug him or whatever. They took the hint and didn't try to follow him to his room, although Atsumu could see how disappointed his dad was. The whole ordeal was a little annoying because Atsumu left Osamu’s things in the dorms and took the first train to Tokyo.

Atsumu braced his ass on a nearby windowsill, waiting for his English literature class. A couple of people were there already.

“Don’t brush her off much, Tsumu. And don’t exaggerate your cooking skills either. She will know. I would rather she didn’t come here unannounced.”

“I doubt it, Samu. They would sooner visit you, since they sent you so far from home. I have to report back home like a criminal every three weeks.” He rolled his eyes. “I have to wiggle out of it somehow, I just don’t know how!”

“We’ll figure something out.”

“How is Sunarin? Still in destructive mode?”

The academic year has barely started and Suna was still a walking disaster.

“Apart from the fact that he burned his own and our instructor’s eyebrows, no.” Atsumu snorted. “Sometimes I think that he wants to be kicked out, but his puppy eyes soften everybody’s hearts.”

“Including yours?” Atsumu moved his eyebrows suggestively.

“I’ve gotta go,” Osamu disconnected all of a sudden.

Atsumu laughed.

The door to the classroom opened and the students shuffled inside. Atsumu realised that Sakusa was one of them and he had to hide somehow, because Atsumu hadn’t seen him at all. He sat somewhere in the back and rolled his eyes at the curly-haired Alpha who sat in the second row (the first one was empty). What a drag.

The class was supposed to be held in Japanese, at least in theory, but the professor decided to run it in the target language and gave them a lot of info in English, ignoring some panicked looks.

“I didn’t think I would see you here,” Atsumu spoke to Sakusa, catching up with him after class. They had only half an hour to the afternoon practise, so he doubted the Alpha headed anywhere but the locker room. “Do you study something connected to literature?”

Sakusa was visibly hunched, with hands digging deep into the pockets of a hoodie so vibrant Atsumu wanted to stab himself in the eyes with chopsticks. He had no idea how he could miss this walking road sign, plus his face mask was so characteristic…

Taking into account that Sakusa was almost two meters tall and his pinched eyebrows made his face look fucking miserable, no wonder people parted before him like the Red Sea.

Fucking weirdo.

“Business,” he answered laconically. “This class is just for satisfying my curiosity and gaining some extra points.”

“Wow, okay. Does it mean you can speak English?”

Sakusa nodded. “I have a C1 certificate. I have had extra lessons since I was five years old. What about you? You don’t look like a literature lover.”

Wow, I’ve been promoted, Atsumu thought sarcastically. He asked me a question.

“English philology but I’m here for soccer,” he admitted. “English was always easy for me. I chose it, hoping I wouldn’t have to study a lot.”

Sakusa nodded with understanding. “I’ve seen your games in high school. Your brother and you had a really nice teamwork. I thought he would play at university level.”

“Ah… Our parents didn’t let Tsumu continue.”

“He’s not playing anymore?”

Atsumu shook his head. “There’s no place for Omegas at the university in Osaka.” Sakusa frowned. “What?”

“Nothing.”

They left it at that. Soon they reached the locker room. Sakusa opened the door and let Atsumu pass first. Atsumu looked at him, confused, but didn’t say anything at this strange behavior.

The practice was a one-way ticket to hell. The excitement of starting university at a prestigious university wore off, leaving only nerves, stress and exhaustion. More than a half of the players didn’t make it in expected time and had to run laps for the rest of the practice. It meant they didn’t have enough players to play a mini-match and were forced to do drills for much longer than they wanted to. Atsumu hated being the guy in the middle of a triangle trying to get the ball from the three guys passing it to each other. He felt bullied like hell, running from one to the other in hope he would get the fucking ball. The fact that Tendou, Ushijima and Sakusa were in his team made it twice as bad, diminishing his chances of getting the ball effortlessly. Atsumu liked challenges but it only irritated him.

“Remember that tomorrow we see each other at seven in the common room for our socializing event!” the captain shouted after they finished practice. “No exceptions! If somebody doesn’t come, they will be running laps for all practices for the next two weeks!”

Atsumu walked back to the dorms, leaving Bokuto with Kuroo somewhere along the way. Kuroo looked at Atsumu suggestively a couple of times, but the Omega just made a disgusted face. Kuroo seemed amused by his reaction.

Taking advantage of some peace and quiet, he sat down at his desk. Four days of university were enough to acquire a big pile of homework. The syllabuses from grammar and literature were bursting at the seams, and he felt faint just from thinking about it. He might have miscalculated the workload for these studies.

He managed to do most of it before Bokutio came back. He opened the door so hard that it hit the wall with a loud bang. Thank God someone glued a special plastic to the wall in order to protect the paint from the handle, otherwise they would have a hole right through.

“Hey, hey, hey! What are you doing?!”

“Homework. I want to practice on the weekend.”

“Seriously?!” Bokuto looked at him pleadingly. “Can I practice with you?!”

“Sure. Maybe one goalkeeper would like to join?”

“I will ask around! Do you wanna watch Netflix?”

Atsumu closed the notebook, more than done with English grammar. “Sure.”

Bokuto made space for Atsumu on his bed and turned on his laptop. Atsumu took his Vabo-chan and put him under his head, making himself comfortable at the Alpha’s bed. They decided to watch ‘Pacific Rim’, because neither of them had seen it and it had great reviews.

Atsumu was a little surprised by Bokuto’s readiness to be close to him. He knew he would be careful to keep some distance with a gay person, not because he would want to be mean, but because he wouldn’t want to send mixed signals. Bouto didn’t look bothered in the slightest and he welcomed Atsumu in his personal space.

Which was nice. Atsumu missed human contact. Omegas were wired that way. They craved close contact with others. Atsumu usually used Osamu to satisfy those needs, bracing his head on Osamu’s shoulder when they watched something or taking his clothes from his wardrobe. Osamu always complained but he never protested, because Omegas, especially healthy and happy ones, had a calming influence on Alphas. Osamu often scent-marked him, warning off other Alphas.

“Bokuto?”

“Yeah? Oh! Whoa, so cool!” Bokuto’s eyes were round, watching two Jaegers fight with Kaiju on the screen. “Being a pilot like that would be so cool!”

Atsumu murmured with agreement, bracing his chin on Bokuto’s shoulder.

“What do you like about Akaashi?” he asked with curiosity.

He wondered since his talk with the Omega.

“Ugh… But you won’t laugh?”

“I won’t.”

“Kuroo always says that but he laughs anyway.”

“I’m not Kuroo. Don’t worry.”

Bokuto bit his bottom lip, lowering his eyes shyly. “Kaashi is just great!” he admitted with cheeks visibly reddening. “He’s super intelligent and was one of the best students in high school! And he can play the violin, and understands all the complicated things in books and is just so, so nice and helpful even if his face looks kinda mean sometimes. And— and he has this sarcastic sense of humor which disorients people at first but Kasshi is never mean, you know? And he can play soccer and is just so, so beautiful!”

Christ , Atsumu thought completely taken aback. He fell head over heels for Akaashi. 

“He was your kouhai in high school, right? Why didn’t you talk to him then?”

Bokuto started playing with his fingers, clearly nervous. “Are you joking? He was one of the most beautiful Omegas at our school! And he comes from this old, traditional Japanese family and is super rich. His family wouldn’t let me be his chauffeur, let alone a potential mate. I’m just so stupid and simple-minded for him… But you can always dream, right?”

“So… it’s not because you just want to tap him?” Atsumu moved his eyebrows suggestively and smirked.

Bokuto waved his arms, almost knocking off the laptop from their laps. “What?! Course not!” His face was beetroot-red. “I’ve never—,” he stopped and gulped.” Have you—? You know?”

Atsumu summoned all possible powers to keep his face in neutral color, but it didn’t work very well. He could feel his face getting hot. “I think you should try,” he said evasively. “Show him that you are a good Alpha.”

Even if Akaashi was biased, Atsumu still thought that it didn’t really matter. Bokuto was an open and honest person. He was sure they could be a good couple.

“Do you really think I have a chance?” Bokuto asked with hope.

“I have no idea,” Atsumu replied honestly. “I don’t get girls and Omegas. But wouldn’t it be better to just see for yourself and be sure? If he doesn’t like you, at least you will know.”

“Maybe— maybe you’re right. Would you help me?”

“Yeah, of course.”

“Thanks, Miya, you’re the best!”

“I hope so!”

With big smiles they went back to watching the movie. Atsumu moved even closer to the Alpha, feeling that they just made their bond deeper. It made him very happy.

The next day the whole team gathered, playing games that their captain and some of his friends had prepared. Atsumu expected some alkohol snuggled in and drunken-games, but they actually spent the evening playing board games, truth or dare, spinning the bottle with some unique rules. Atsumu learned a lot of things about his teammates. For starters, Sakusa and Komori were cousins, Kuroo had met his boyfriend by breaking his nose with a volleyball. Bokuto was the only male member of his family, Tendou liked making chocolates in his free time… Ushijima was allergic to strawberries, and Oikawa, who appeared out of thin air (he wasn’t there before because of his injury), believed in aliens. Atsumu just said he couldn’t cook.

“I still can’t believe you’re cousins,” he said, looking at Sakusa and Komori. “You don’t look similar at all, and your personalities are literally like day and night.”

Komori was a friendly, cheerful brown-haired Beta, with two dots imitating eyebrows and mischievous gleam in his eyes. Sakusa was a fucking grump with eternal scowl, a mop of wild, raven curls and eyes so dark they were almost black. He had those twin moles over his right eyebrow. Apart from their different looks, both had totally different aura. 

“Everybody tells us that. Our mothers are sisters,” Komori explained. “We both took after our fathers more.”

Although the meeting was for everybody, mainly first and second years took part in it. Atsumu noticed right away that the older players looked bored and weren’t very forthcoming with the information about themselves. Maybe it was a direct result of the fact it wasn’t their first time, or maybe they just weren’t happy that so many talented players joined the team. Whatever it was, it didn’t discourage Atsumu in the slightest. He was amused by their childish behavior and couldn’t wait to take their spot in the first line.

On Saturdays most of the buildings were closed on campus, but the cafeteria and sports facilities weren't. Atsumu took advantage of that, using the gym in the morning for his strength training before he went to get some food. The prices in the cafeteria were okay, but he knew it was too expensive for him anyway, so eating there all the time was out of the question. He just wanted to enjoy it till it lasted.

Akaashi was already there in his favorite spot. He had a company Atsumu didn’t know, but he decided to join them anyway.

“Hi, Akaashi,” he greeted the Omega. “Mind if I join?”

“Miya-san, hi.” Atsumu sat down on the free chair. “This is Iwaizumi-san. We share a room at dorms. Iwaizumi-san, this is Miya, our soccer team’s new member.”

Atsumu greeted Iwaizumi with a nod. The guy was frowning. He had short, spiky hair, green eyes and a face like a delinquent. He looked intimidating. “Nice to meet you!” he added with a big grin.

“How was the team meeting? I heard the whole team went there?” Akaashi asked.

“It was cool. I don’t remember the last time I played board games. Kuroo cheated in Monopoly.”

“So I’ve heard.”

“Sakusa complained?”

“‘Complained’ is a little too much, but— yeah.”

Akaashi changed the topic, including them both in conversation. It turned out that Iwaizumi studied sports medicine and wanted to be an athletic trainer. Atsumu got instantly interested and asked him many questions. Iwaizumi had, as it turned out, great knowledge about exercises, proper stretching and massages for athletes. He was a goldmine of info. Atsumu wasn’t even sure how much time they talked.

In the afternoon, he went shopping. He bought a lot of instant ramen and some stuff that even he could cook easily. Osamu could supervise him over the phone.

After shopping, Bokuto called him to the pitch. He managed to collect eight people in total, which was enough to play many popular soccer games. Someone brought portable speakers, blasting music loudly. They had a great time, fooling around and dancing after each nice play. Atsumu felt truly alive, kicking the ball with other boys. He couldn’t wait for his call with Osamu, he wanted to tell him about everything.

On Sunday, he went with Bokuto to arcades and sightsee the city. Bokuto turned out to be a great guide. He knew a lot about the history of many tourist places. He told him many funny stories about his own shenanigans. After a long walk around the city center, they stopped at a small izakaya for food, wolfing it down and then ice-cream shortly after. He talked a lot about soccer and tactics. Atsumu had a lot of ideas for different plays, each practice letting him get to know the players better and plan accordingly.

The second week in Tokyo made Atsumu slowly get used to everything. He also realised how expensive it was to feed two growing boys. He and Osamu had literally eaten through most of their savings. Atsumu had no idea how they were going to survive in the long run. They have been talking about the problem, settling on Osamu getting a job. They had no other choice. Even with Suna sharing his food with Osamu — who cooked for them both in turn — their expenses were simply too big. And Atsumu didn’t even buy stuff that he couldn’t cook anyway.

He started to appreciate all the times Osamu cooked for him without complaints.

____________

“— and then he screamed and started demolishing the room,” Sakusa said calmly, turning his paper cup in hands. Atsumu had noticed him right after he turned the last corner. The Alpha was sitting on the wide windowsill, keeping his distance from the rest of the group. Atsumu didn’t hesitate and just went to him, because even though he still thought Sakusa was crazy, he was kinda funny and totally harmless. And, of course, Atsumu was dying to know what had happened the day before between him and his roommate that they made a big fuss after midnight that almost ended in a fist fight. “He didn’t like the fact that his kouhai dared to reprimand him. When he realized I wasn’t going to back off, he tried to hit me. Wakatoshi-kun stopped him. Then the captain came, alerted by the whole commotion.”

“And? What did you tell him?”

Sakusa sighed, frustrated. “The same Fukuri heard… That we don’t live in a pig pen and we share the space, so expecting some cleaning from time to time isn’t high demands. The captain said I exaggerate. Exaggerate .” Sakusa was very displeased. Atsumu nodded to each comment, but he kind of agreed with the captain. Sakusa wasn’t exactly subtle about the fact that he was a stickler for cleanliness. He never let anybody touch him, he wore masks all the time and beat everybody to the showers in the morning. He didn’t even want to shake hands and declined any and all human contact after scoring a goal. The only time he accepted somebody’s touch was during the mandatory stretches that they had in pairs, but even then he made all his partners disinfect their hands beforehand. That kind of behavior repulsed a lot of players on the team. Atsumu wasn’t surprised that the captain took Fukuri’s side in a blink of an eye. “Apparently asking him to wash hands after coming back, picking up his stinky, dirty underwear from my side of the room , wiping out the shower stall from water and pubic hair, and washing the dishes after using the stuff in the kitchen is too much. I don’t even want to think about the three-day-old pizza that he kept on his bedside table ‘for later’ and all the crumbs he had on his sheets…” The Alpha shivered in disgust. “He’s a pig.”

Okay, maybe he wasn’t exaggerating.

“He was the one who was leaving all the dirty dishes in the kitchen? Bokuto complained that someone was taking his stuff and never washed it, so he had to do it himself if he wanted to cook something.”

“Mhm. Wakatoshi-kun backed me up and said that Fukuri doesn't clean at all and one of us has to always clean after him. Coming from a wealthy family doesn’t justify that kind of behavior. But even with Wakatoshi’s support, the captain was still backing this pig up. In the end it was decided that Fukuri will move to the captain’s room.”

“Well… Then let’s see how quickly he regrets that decision,” Atsumu joked.

Sakusa smiled slightly. “Yeah, that’s not my problem anymore. I think he shouldn’t coddle him, but I can’t say I’m not happy with the way it ended.”

“For sure. You have a room for yourself.”

Atsumu liked Bokuto but he wouldn’t hesitate to kick him out for good if he had the chance. He could feel much more comfortable on his own. Pretending to be Osamu was laughingly easy, and the suppressants and scent blockers were doing their job, but he still couldn’t relax fully. Maybe in a couple of weeks, when he falls into a proper routine, he will be able to relax.

Their conversation was interrupted by the professor who opened the door to the classroom for them. They went inside with the rest of the group and the class started. Atsumu refused sitting in the front, and Sakusa didn’t even want to think about sitting in the back, so they separated in the classroom and took their previous spots. But after the class covering their first reading assignment they had to complete in two weeks, they met outside the class and headed together to the locker room.

Suddenly, someone shouted Sakusa’s name out loud. The Alpha looked over his shoulder and quickened his pace. Atsumu glanced at him with puzzlement.

“Sakusa-kun! I know you can hear me. Stop right this second!”

He didn’t. The man had to literally bar Sakusa’s path. The guy took a deep breath, murmuring about ‘damn athletes’. “Join us!” he said, cutting to the chase. “You could bring so much onto the stage!”

“Why me?” Sakusa asked. It looked like he knew the guy.

“Your performance was genius!”

“No, it wasn’t.”

“We need you.”

“You don’t.”

“You will develop artistically!”

“I don’t want to,” he deadpanned. He blinked and pointed at Atsumu. “And I don’t have time. Miya needs help with English, I promised I would teach him,” he lied through his teeth.

“Hey, you didn—” Atsumu whined when Sakusa’s elbow hit him in the side. “Ugh.”

“Think about it. I offer extra credit, it’s the amount for two classes. You just need to show up twice a week for practice, and on the weekends before the show.”

“There are no points for drama club.”

“But there are from the history of Japanese literature which is taught by my wife.”

“Why me? I don’t even practice anymore.”

“You know every piece we need. The choreography isn’t difficult, someone with so much experience would get it for sure. Your performance proved it would be a piece of cake for you.”

“I don’t dance,” Sakusa was scandalized.

Atsumu had seen a tennis match once and it felt a lot like it.

“You don’t have to dance.”

“I can manage English on my own,” Atsumu interrupted, purposefully throwing him to the wolves. He looked at Sakusa innocently, giggling inside like a schoolgirl. “It looks like such a good offer, you can’t miss out on all the fun!”

The man clapped his hands. “Awesome! The rehearsals are Tuesdays and Fridays at three in building G. I checked, you’re free. See you tomorrow! Bye!”

Before any of them had a chance to react, the man ran away like a murderer from the crime scene. Sakusa looked pissed, so Atsumu started withdrawing in a very unsuspicious way.

“Miya, you’re dead!”

Laughing loudly, Atsumu sprinted through the hall. To his great surprise and amusement, Sakusa ran right after him with murder clear in his eyes.

______________

The third week at the university started badly. Atsumu tried to postpone his visit at home, exaggerating the number of tasks he had to complete, but his mum was stern and hell bent on bringing him home. After buying tickets they almost ran out of money for food, which they realised on a bright Tuesday morning.

“I’m hungry!” Osamu complained with an unhappy face. “My stomach is growling.”

“Not only you, scrub,” Atsumu whined. “I didn’t eat supper yesterday!”

“Maybe Suna will share with me,” Osamu was thinking out loud. “We have to learn how to manage our money better.”

Definitely. With a stomach tight from hunger he thought miserably that he could say ‘no’ to arcades with Bokuto and sweets he had bought. He wouldn’t have to deal with it now.

“Take the rest, Samu,” Atsumu said. Osamu was much more food-oriented than Atsumu. He could eat at home on Friday, so Osamu could spend the money they had left.

Maybe going home wouldn’t be so bad after all.

Ignoring the guilt trying to swallow him whole, he entered the kitchen and went through his floormates' stuff. Most of them had some food there. Ushijima used his space for storing sports drinks, two guys from the end of the hall had some food containers, and Bokuto had a big bowl of rice and curry. Apologizing to him in his mind, he took enough to sate his hunger. The food was so delicious he almost cried. He inhaled it and drank a lot of coffee to fill his stomach. 

He knew he wouldn’t survive the rest of the week like that, not with all the soccer practice he had scheduled. With reductance he decided to borrow some money and give it back when Osamu gets his first paycheck.

He thought about going to Bokuto, but his roommate was constantly out of money and borrowed from Kuroo. Akaashi was a nice friend to bitch with about life, but they usually saw each other in the cafeteria and that was the last place Atsumu wanted to go to. When he saw Sakusa near the entrance to the dorms, he made up his mind. He took a deep breath and went to the dark-haired Alpha.

Sakusa was still a little mad about the stunt Atsumu pulled with the drama club and for a guy who didn’t talk much, his eyebrows and eyes were very expressive about his displeasure. Atsumu had even apologized, half-serious, half-joking, but it didn't satisfy the prickly striker. Sakusa was totally offended by this betrayal and stopped ignoring Atsumu after whole days of judging him with his eyebrows.

“Hi,” Atsumu greeted him. Sakusa’s face fell when he realised who was standing before him. “I’m happy I see you, too.”

“What do you want, Miya? I’m busy.”

Atsumu wanted to tease him a little like always, but bit his tongue. He looked the Alpha in the eyes pleadingly. “Would you lend me some money? I promise I will give it back.”

He didn't say what he needed the money for. He felt embarrassed that he had to borrow some for food.

Sakusa frowned. He was silent for a long moment. Atsumu lost hope he could get any help from him when the Alpha reached to his canvas backpack and took 10 000 ¥ out of his wallet. He gave it to Atsumu.

“Is it all?”

Atsumu took the money, his cheeks reddening slightly. “Thank you,” he said softly.

“Sure. See you in practice.”

Atsumu nodded.

Biting his thumb, he started researching smart ways of budgeting the grocery shopping. He learned a lot of interesting stuff that he never had had to worry about, because his parents might not be rich, but they weren’t poor either. He learned that the key to success was planning meals one whole week in advance, which was problematic for Atsumu, because he couldn’t cook! With a martyr expression on his face he somehow managed to plan each meal till Friday. Most of them consisted of instant soup which absolutely saved money, but started to be disgusting and unbearable.

Some articles mentioned making a list of necessary items and buying only them. Checking the expiration date. Looking for sales and discounts. Buying bigger products if you paid for an item not how much it weighed. Setting a budget and sticking to it. And absolutely avoiding going grocery shopping while hungry. Cooking for more than one person because it’s less expensive.

Easy peasy. He even knew how to make sure he would eat great, home-cooked meals.

“Bokuto? What would you say for a small deal?” he proposed in the evening, when they were getting ready to go to sleep.

“Deal?” the Alpha tilted his head. His hair was down, bouncing off his forehead and cheeks freely, changing his image completely. Bokuto at first didn’t want him to see him this way but Atsumu managed to convince him.

“Do you remember that I promised to praise you in front of Akaashi?” Bokuto nodded. “I will introduce you and make sure you won’t make an idiot out of yourself.”

Too big of an idiot, anyway, he added in his head.

Bokuto looked at him suspiciously. “What do you want in return?”

“I know you cook for yourself most meals. I want you to cook for both of us and we can split the groceries in half.”

Bokuto blinked. “You want to eat my food?” he asked, surprised.

“I can’t cook! And eating home-cooked meals is healthier and cheaper than eating in the cafeteria.”

Bokuto smiled. “Sure, no problem! Cooking for one person is so sad! We can share!”

Dear God, if you exist, bless this big-hearted moron.

“Sad?”

“I always cooked for everybody at home! It’s so strange to cook just for myself, I can’t figure out the proper portions.”

“You’re the best, Bokkun.”

“Bokkun?”

“Can I call you that?”

“A nickname?! Sure! Of course!”

Atsumu wanted to hug him. They quickly figured out the details of grocery shopping and Atsumu’s eating preferences. After starving he had to endure on Tuesday, it was difficult to be picky. He already knew what it was to have no options at all.

On Thursday, the English literature class was cancelled at the last minute. The professor had to fall ill in the middle of the day or something. His absence resulted in Atsumu and Sakuda heading to the locker room one and a half hours earlier.

As they expected, there was nobody there. Atsumu changed into his sports gear and ran to the bathroom, whereas Sakusa dug out their footballs out of the basket — everybody had their own signed even though it was prohibited — and pumped them.

“Miya, your phone is ringing!” Sakusa shouted to him.

“Who is it?” Atsumu replied from the bathroom.

“Food Stealing Runt written with a mistake?”

“What? What mistake?”

“It should be a Food-Stealing Runt. Otherwise it seems as if the food is the one stealing runts?”

“Ugh, fine, I will correct it later. Anyway, it’s my twin, ignore him.”

“He wrote a message.” Atsumu entered the locker room. Sakusa was still watching his screen. “‘Code red. Don’t pick up from mum’ written in all caps.”

“What?” Atsumu took his phone and frowned.

Food Stealing Runt : CODE RED! DON’T PICK UP FROM MUM!!!!

Food Stealing Runt : !!!

At the same time, his phone started ringing, showing ‘MaMa Miya’ on the screen. Atsumu scratched his cheek. Sakusa looked at him with raised eyebrows.

“You won’t pick up?” he asked with a smirk.

“It doesn’t look like a good idea. I wonder what Samu— Tsumu had done,” he corrected quickly and cleared his throat. When the phone got silent, Atsumu called his twin instantly.

“We have a problem,” was the first thing coming out of Osamu’s mouth.

Atsumu turned his back to Sakusa. “I figured. What happened?”

“I had a small accident in today’s classes. Can you switch on your camera?”

Atsumu smiled at Sakusa apologetically and exited the locker room. He braced his back on the wall near the door and looked around to make sure nobody was there.

“You are talking to me, so it can’t be that bad, right? You didn’t cut off any fingers?”

“No, but—,” Osamu switched on his camera and showed Atsumu the back of his hand. Osamu’s right hand was angry-red and swollen, covered in painful-looking blisters. “I have this.”

“Was it Suna?” Atsumu asked harshly.

“It was an accident,” Osamu dodged the question.

“If it was Suna—”

“It wasn’t Sunarin’s fault, okay?” Osamu snapped, losing his patience. “I mean, it was his milk, but one girl tripped and pushed him into me. It’s a kitchen, that kind of thing happens all of the time. Stop nagging. The problem is, our instructor forced me to go to the nurse, and they put it into my file as a second degree burn.”

And notified the Alpha , Atsumu thought.

“Samu, I’m going home tomorrow!”

“I fucking know!”

Did he? Atsumu couldn’t just show up without the burns, it would raise too many questions. And making Osamu go won’t work. Their mum could tell them apart no matter what, she just needed to look to be aware of which one of them was it.

“I tried to wiggle out of it. Mum said I have to bring my ass home, otherwise dad will drag me there himself.”

“That’s the last thing I want to deal with. Maybe we should try to cover it with some make-up?”

“You want to trick a former EMT with make-up?”

“Fuck. You’re right. One thing is sure, I can’t go home this week.” Atsumu looked at him incredulously. “What? I can’t show up there with my burned hand!”

“I wanted to see you, you fucker! I didn't think I would miss your ugly mug!”

“We have the same face, loser.”

“I wear it better.”

They both sighed in unison and fell silent, each one of them in deep thought. Atsumu was looking forward to seeing his twin. He didn’t think he would miss him so much, but he couldn’t break the habit of turning to him after so many years of living out of each other’s pockets. Atsumu was used to sharing everything with his twin, even if the lack of privacy and space sent him up the wall sometimes. Without Osamu next to him he felt as if he had lost one limb.

“If I have to go there, there is only one solution,” Atsumu said, biting his bottom lip.

Osamu’s eyes filled with anxiety. “Are you sure?”

“You know that bandaging my hand won’t stop mum from looking at it. She will want to see it. You say it was milk?”

Osamu bit his thumb-nail, unhappy. “I don't like it, Tsumu.”

“Then figure something else out. I have to go, Sakusa is waiting for me. We will talk in the evening, okay?”

“Okay.”

They finished their conversation at that. Atsumu sighed and tucked his phone in his pocket before returning to the locker room. Sakusa was waiting for him with his hand in his pockets, juggling the soccer ball with his feet.

“I’m back. sorry I made you wait.”

“Is everything all right?”

“Yeah, Atsumu had a small adventure in one of his classes. Nothing serious, but you know how mothers react,” he brushed him off with a shrug. “Ready?”

Sakusa looked at him weirdly, but nodded anyway and they went to the pitch.

Till the evening Atsumu was mulling over the problem in his head. He tried to find another solution, but nothing came to his mind, so he was left with the first and last idea of dealing with the problem. That’s why he went to the kitchen at a quite late hour, ready to carry out the plan. Osamu was watching over him from the screen with a blank face.

“Ready?” asked Atsumu.

“I should ask you that. Are you sure you want to do it?”

“I won’t let something like that get in my way,” he replied gruffly, heating up the milk.

“I’m sorry, Tsumu.”

“That’s not your style, Samu, so shut up. You told me yourself, it was an accident. It was just a matter of time for one of us to harm himself.”

“Tsumu?”

“What”

“You better not break a leg.”

Atsumu snorted. “I will try my best.”

When the milk was hot enough, Atsumu took a deep breath. He brought the pot over his hand and outstretched his hand over the sink. He tilted the pot a little.

“Hey, Miya”!

Atsumu jerked back and milk spilt all over his outstretched hand. Even though that was the plan from the very beginning, it didn’t hurt any less. He inhaled deeply, feeling the hot liquid on the back of his hand and wrist. The Alpha standing in the door to the kitchen was watching the whole thing with horrified eyes. Atsumu didn’t think that Kuroo could look so aghast.

“Jesus Christ!” Kuroo was next to him in a blink of an eye. “Miya, I’m so sorry, I didn't want to startle you. “Kuroo gripped his forearm and brought it closer to himself, inspecting the burn with a guilty expression. It looked awful. “Fuck.”

“Do you want me to get a heart attack?” Atsumu asked. He moaned when the Alpha started wetting the burn with lukewarm water.

“I’m sorry. What were you doing with the milk anyway?”

“I wanted to pour it into my mug for hot cocoa,” Atsumu lied. He winced. The burn stung like hell. Kuroo changed the temperature to colder one.

“Keep cooling it down, I will be back in a sec.”

When he left, Atsumu sighed.

“What a timing,” Osamu murmured. Atsumu showed him his hand. “It looks terrible.”

“I hope I won’t have a scar.”

“It shouldn’t scar. The color may be slightly different though.”

The door opened with a loud bang. Atsumu quickly said goodbye to his twin, focusing on Bokuto and Sakusa who entered the kitchen. Sakusa had a small first aid kit in his hand. Bokuto inhaled dramatically, seeing Atsumuls hand, covered in blisters popping out of thin air. Kuroo tried to explain himself clumsily.

“You will buy me dinner and we’re even,” Atsumu proposed. “And start saving up for a surgery bleaching my skin to its normal color because I don’t wanna to look like a freaking Frankenstein.”

Kuroo snorted, but agreed easily. Sakusa opened the first aid kit and made Atsumu sit next to himself.

“I thought you study business?” Atsumu said.

“My parents and siblings are all doctors,” he replied easily. “I know more about first aid than I would like to.”

“Hmm, makes sense.”

Kuroo and Bokuto were discussing something, checking on Atsumu every few minutes with worried expressions. Sakusa dried his hand delicately before he put some ointment on it and covered it with a bizarre looking band-aid. He made sure the edges weren’t peeling off.

“All done. The band-aid is waterproof, but try to keep it dry anyway. If it won’t get worse, you can skip going to the doctor. You can just spray it with that. “He gave Atsumu a small bottle of Panthenol . “It should soothe some of the pain. And know you can just take this.” He gave him some painkillers. Atsumu took one right away, sure that he would need all the help he could get.

“Thank you, Doctor Sakusa,” Atsumu said with a big grin.

Sakusa winced. Atsumu didn’t even have to see his face — the Alpha was wearing a face-mask — to know that. Sakusa’s dark gaze was grinding into him intensively. Atsumu blinked, not sure what warranted such an intense look.

The next day he peeled off the band-aid and splayed it with Panthenol just as Sakusa told him to. It helped, and Atsumu was really glad for it because it hurt like a bitch. After some time Atsumu put on another band-aid from the Alpha and went to his first class. Bokuto prepared a delicious onigiri for them. Atsumu wasn’t able to eat all of it — he was leaving for the train in a bit — so he shared with Akaashi who turned out to be a big hog and could eat his weight in food.

His parents shook their heads at him when they saw the burns. They said it was inevitable, taking into account his culinary skills or lack thereof. When they asked — again — how the hell did he manage to pass the entrance exams (did he cheat?), he told him the same story Osamu heard from Suna: he changed each ‘C’ to ‘K’ and ticked the answers on a way to get BAKA repeatedly. His dad smacked him up the head for it. The burn, as it turned out, saved him from showing off his newly-acquired cooking skills. And even though he was still mad at her for putting him through such bullshit for her misplaced ambition, he played a good son and she gave him a lot of food ready to just heat-up as well as money for new shoes and a nice hoodie.

He set all the money aside and put it into their secret banking account, happy they could use it later for buying food.

Chapter 4

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

After seven weeks of being a student, Atsumu could honestly say he got used to his new routine and quite liked it. On Mondays, Tuesdays, and Wednesdays, he attended his classes, then spent his lunch hour working on his homework in Akaashi’s company — sometimes Iwaizumi’s, too, and even the mysterious Kenma who played some games all the time and barely talked — and then went to more classes and to practice. Then he usually watched something with Bokuto or spent time with guys from his floor in the kitchen or the meeting room. On Thursdays, he spent time, surprisingly, with Sakusa. They went for coffee about an hour before their shared literature class (they were both free and bored), and then they went hand in hand to the afternoon practice. He hesitated, eyebrows raising at a scuffle on the other side. He knew the sounds well since Atsumu and Osamu always fought over the phone when he called them to ask how the competition was going.

“Miya-san? It’s Sakusa Kiyoomi.” A deep, velvety vioce said into the phone. “You saw me at the campus. I’m Atsumu’s boyfriend.” Haruo blinked, taken aback. What was Atsumu’s boyfriend doing in an Omega’s clinic? “I understand that you don’t know me and my words probably don’t mean much to you, but please, don’t stop Atsumu from playing. He’s the best playmaker I’ve ever seen and I know what I’m talking about. He hung up and sighed.

He agreed to all her propositions and suggestions, because he knew how much she loved and adored them. It was obvious she didn’t have malicious intentions, but was her idea of happiness overlapping with the boys’? Atsumu inherited her explosive temper, yet not materialism. She always wanted to be a lady, invite girlfriends for coffee, tell others how to live their lives. Even though they were doing fine financially, Haruo wasn’t able to give her that standard of life. Maybe she wanted someone rich for Atsumu so she could get that way of living through him? He truly didn’t know.

But, what was important was the fact that Atsumu was not interested in that. The money always burnt a hole in his pocket. The moment he had it, he spent it, and when he didn’t, he shrugged and didn’t care. The way he and Osamu decided to work behind their backs and how they earned enough for all their expenses made him realize they were responsible adults. And sure, they still had a lot of things to learn, bur they matured in the blink of an eye.

His inner debate was stopped by Akari who came back much calmer. One of her trusted friends was a pharmacist and probably talked her down.

“Now?” he asked her.

“I don’t want to stress over it,” she told him, going up the stairs. He groaned and followed her. “Atsumu!” Knocking on the door, she pushed the door and went inside before either of the twins could answer. They were both on the bottom bunk, their eyes puffy and red. “I’m not pregnant!”

“We’re just gonna check.” Atsumu didn’t move a muscle. Akari sighed, rubbing her face. “I’m not going to fight with you over this. Come on.”

“I won’t pee in front of you. Osamu can come with me.”

“No way. How am I supposed to know he won’t pee there instead of you?” 

“I won’t do it in front of you.”

“You peed in front of me for years, you can do it now. I’m the only Omega here anyway.”

Atsumu looked at his dad pleadingly. He instantly caught the hint.

“Maybe I’ll go with you?” he proposed. “I promise not to look.”

Surprisingly, Atsumu seemed relieved by that.

Akari, not so much.

“So what? I’m the problem now? Thanks a lot, Tsumu!”

Haruo followed Atsumu to the bathroom and closed the door. As he had promised, he turned his back to his son in order to give him some privacy. Atsumu fought with the package for a moment before he proceeded to read the instruction. Then Haruo heard him unzip his pants and pee. He pet his shoulder, trying to reassure him that everything would be okay. It had worked like a magic in the past, but this time Atsumu didn’t seem to react to it, quite the opposite actually. He tensed up as if readying himself for a fight.

“It’s gonna be fine,” he told him.

Atsumu hunched his shoulders and stayed silent.

The test was negative, which was a huge relief, even though he would never admit to it.

“I’ll make a doctor’s appointment for you just in case,” Akari said.

“There is no need,” Haruo interfered. “I called Atsumu’s doctor in Tokyo. She said he’s fit as a fiddle.”

“And these pseudo-suppressants? We’re just supposed to trust her word? God knows what they’ve been giving him.”

“It’s a private clinic, the best in Tokyo, actually. Doctor Nobuki is also one of the best specialists there.”

“He started having sex—”

“Still a damn virgin. From both sides,” Atsumu said, smirking.

“Fuck off, Tsumu! It’s all your damn fault!” Osamu swatted him in the back, angry and red as a tomato.

“It’s so not. I told you to tell him the truth.”

“Ah! So you’re also seeing someone?” Haruo asked with interest.

Osamu sent Atsumu a seething glare and nodded reluctantly.

“Do we know him?”

Both twins shook their heads.

They dropped the topic for the rest of the day. Akari confiscated their phones, annoyed with the way they both had been trying to text under the table. That shut them both up totally and neither one of them uttered a single word during the entire course of the meal. They were both hungry, but the situation and tense atmosphere made them lose their appetites.

Haruo didn’t have it that easy, though. Akari almost bore him to death with her ideas about finding Atsumu an Alpha, showing him pictures of the candidates she’d selected. Atsumu’s boyfriend hadn’t made the list.

Haruo didn't like to rush his decisions. He knew that emotions were logic’s false friends. He was the type of person who liked to sleep on the problem and that one wasn’t any different.

The next day, ho woke up, and after the emotions lost their intensity and common sense came back, he had an idea of what he should do.

Not telling everybody, he went to the train station and bought a ticket to Tokyo. On his way there, he made a phone call and took a day off due to a family emergency. He blamed it all on the twins which wasn’t unusual. Whenever he said there was a family emergency it was usually because of the twins. Everybody knew about his two troublemakers and they long had gotten used to it.

He seemed pretty lucky because he made it to the university right at the same time as the rector himself. Atsumu’s case was big enough to address it instantly and the man let him into his office, ready to discuss it. The coach and the year’s tutor were called in as well.

“No way,” the Beta said right away. “It’s against the rules.”

“Yes way!” the coach opposed. “That’s one of the best playmakers I’ve coached! The kid’s got talent and dedication to make it far in this sport! I won’t some sleazy asshole ruin that for any of us.”

“Talented or not, he’s not above the rules! We’re an establishment with hundreds of years worth of traditions! And you want to trash it for one troublemaker?”

The rector’s eyes jumped from one man to the othe as if he was watching a tennis match. Eventually, he sighed tiredly.

“There are always problems with Omegas,” he murmured to the tutor’s glee. “There was one when we first started taking them in, there’s now and there always will be.” He looked at Atsumu’s records, looking through his grades and achievements. “The grades seem fine, although they could have been better. But, considering he had to work to support himself, I can say they’re decent. His determination is worth… admiration, as well.”

It was the coach’s time to be smug.

“What am I supposed to do with all of you, huh? How did the team react to Miya’s secondary gender?”

The coach shrugged. “Surprisingly good, especially the first and second years. The third and fourth less enthusiastically, but let’s be honest, they will all be gone soon. We have so much potential this time around! Ushijima was already scouted by the Adlers, and Oikawa’s going to Argentina. Bokuto caught the interest of Jackals. My team is a star factory! I want Miya. Ba! I'll gladly take two!”

“Em, sorry, but Osamu wants to be a chef,” Haruo told him with apologetic smile plastered on his face.

“What a shame.”

“So the statute is the problem.”

“But—”

“Usagi-san, I understand your concerns, but it’s the same situation as years ago when the laws changed and Omegas were let here at all. The times are changing. If it was up to me, no Miya or any Omega or woman would set foot in these buildings. But as it is, it’s not my decision. We have a council that rules over matters like that and that’s what will happen this time around as well. I don’t think Miya Atsumu is a danger to anybody here, maybe himself since he’s the sheep among wolves. We will vote on that. If the board agrees, he can come back, continue his education and join the team. If not, he’ll be expelled and able to enroll next year as a regular student without the possibility of playing for the team. This solution should satisfy everybody.”

With these words he ushered them all out of his office. The Beta shrugged and left without a word. The coach murmured something about him being an asshole.

Haruo swapped numbers with the coach and made him promise to contact him when the board voted. The man promised to do just that and left as well, leaving Haruo to his own devices. His mind made, Haruo went to the Alphas’ dorm. He realized, amused, that Osamu probably had waited a few minutes for them to go and then hit the train station to go all the way back.

Nobody tried to stop him from entering. He easily made it up the stairs, the corridors and staircase pretty empty.

“Bokuto-san, you’ll fa—” BOOM. “I told you you’d fall.”

“AGHASHEEEE! They do it in all movies!”

“We talked about it. Movies lie.”

“Not all of them.”

Haruo turned around the corner and noticed a young Omega, and an Alpha in the middle of making it up from the floor. The Omega looked quite tired and slightly irritated, but mostly tired. The Alpha was pouting, his eyes upset.

Haruo realized that he knew them. Bokuto was the Alpha that had shareda room with Atsumu, and the Omega next to him had to be one of his friends. When they saw him, they also recognized him right away.

“Miya-san?” Bokuto asked, tiliting his head like a confused owl. He jumped up, eyes sparkling. “Os… Is Atsumu back?” he asked, excited.

“Ah, hi. Bokuto-kun, Aghashee-kun?”

“Akaashi Keiji,” the Omega corrected politely and bowed. “What brings you here, sir?”

“Ah, I hoped to find… Omi? Atsumu’s boyfriend?”

“He should be in his room! We don’t have classes today,” Bokuto told him eagerly.

“We can take you there,” Akaashi proposed.

“I’d appreciate it.”

As it turned out, Sakusa’s room was on the same corridor as Atsumu’s, just few doors further. Bokuto rammed on the door a few times, yelling Alpha’s name and telling him he had a visitor.

“Bokuto, could you knock like a normal person?” Sakusa asked, opening the door with an unhappy expression on his face. His eyes were narrowed and exasperated.

Haruo took a better look, trying to see him with Atsumu’s eyes. Black, slightly disheveled curls framed his face. He had nicely-shaped eyebrows, dark-brown eyes and straight, aristocratic nose. His lips were thin, cheekbones high, twin moles on his forehead kind of cute.

Haruo’s eyes moved lower, to the neck also covered in small brown spots, then to his obvious athletic physique hidden under a dark T-shirt and loose sweatpants. He was tall. Very. Atsumu and Osamu had grown like weed, but Sakusa had to be even taller, because Haruo had to look up to look him in the eyes.

When the boy noticed him, his frown smoothed out and something like hope shone in his eyes.

“Miya-san, hello,” he said and bowed slightly. He looked behind him. “Is Atsumu—?”

“Ah, no, no, I’m sorry. Atsumu is in Hyogo. Do you have a moment? I’d like to talk with you.”

Sakusa hesitated but moved to the side to let Haruo in. The man knew he had caught him by surprise so he expected the room to be quite messy. What he saw was the exact opposite. The entire room was sparkling clean, all things neatly folded or set on the shelves, the bed made… Nothing looked out of place as if Sakusa had been expecting Haruo’s visit.

Bokuto tried to step inside the room, but Sakusa scowled at him and shut the door in the other Alpha’s face. Bokuto yelped and started complaining it wasn’t nice, but Akaashi distracted him and they were both shortly gone, leaving Haruo and Sakusa alone. Sakusa hunched, his fingers squeezing in the soft fabric of his T-shirt. He looked unsure.

“So? How long you and Atsumu—?” he prompted, looking at the young Alpha.

“A few months,” Sakusa answered. “Although it feels like we’ve been together for ages.”

“Atsumu admitted you two had sex.”

Sakusa tensed, his face and neck turning red at an alarming pace.

“I cannot believe that once again I’m about to have this conversation because of this asshole,” he murmured. “You might not believe me, but it was all Atsumu’s idea.”

Haruo chuckled good-naturedly. “Oh, I totally believe that. It sounds exactly as something Tsumu would do. I didn’t come here to terrorize you over being with my son. You seem reasonable and nice and I hope you really are. Believe it or not, I care about my boys and I want them to be happy.”

“It that is really the case, why isn’t he here? Why can’t he play?”

“I didn’t say that.” Sakusa’s eye rounded. “But it’s not up to me. The university has to approve it first and it’s a big decision. But anyway… I know I’m asking for a lot, but would you like to go with me to Hyogo and surprise Atsumu? He’s really down and it would make his day for sure. Besides, it feels like we need everybody we can get on our side to convince my wife that letting him play is the right thing to do.”

Sakusa didn’t have to be told twice. He asked how long he could stay and then he packed quickly in one of his bags. He needed only twenty minutes to do so. In the meantime, Haruo explained to him that Atsumu’s phone had been taken by Akari and he couldn’t have texted him back in any way. 

Haruo wasn’t sure what to think about Sakusa. The young man was very calm and quiet, a total opposite of Atsumu the loudmouth. He was also weird. He spent the entire way to the train station in a surgical mask and kept in on during the ride, with the exception of the coffee break. He kept hunching while walking as if he was aware of his height and disliked it. He tensed every time Haruo touched him but never protested outwardly. 

Summa summarum, Haruo thought he was nice, albeit quite boring. He showed quite an interesting sense of humor, though. He told Haruo about some funny situations that the twins had gotten themselves into in the past few months. He also admitted how he discovered who Atsumu really was and how they bumped into each other over the years, competing in the same tournaments but rarely facing off.

By accident, he let something else slip as well.

“Your parents’ clinic? The one that Atsumu was going to? You mean that your parents manage it?”

“No, it belongs to my family. My parents have a few hospitals and clinics in the entire country, but the one in Tokyo is the newest and has the best equipment. They always wanted me to follow in their footsteps, so I understand Atsumu well. My family also wasn’t thrilled when they learnt what my plans for the future are. They think soccer is too uncertain and one bad injury could ruin my entire career completely.” He shrugged. “I promised to finish my education before I decide for good, but it doesn’t change anything. I’m good at what I do and I won’t do anything else.”

“And here I took you for a calm and quiet person,” Haruo murmured. “There is a heart of a lion hidden under that aloof facade, huh? No wonder Tsumu likes you so much.”

Sakusa smirked and shrugged.

Before they made it home, they stepped by the university in Osaka to clarify everything for Osamu. The lady in the student’s office almost fainted when she realized that there had been an Alpha living in the Omega dorm. Thankfully, she was pissing herself so much, and was so eager to transfer Osamu where he really belonged that she didn’t even try to threaten them with taking legal actions and it went quite smoothly. After half an hour, Osamu was officially moved to the dorm for Alphas and could continue his studies without problems.

Haruo would be happy to invite Osamu’s partner slash the person that caught his eye, but although Sakusa knew his name, they weren’t able to locate him around the campus. After an hour of useless searching, they gave up and went home.

“Ready?” Haruo asked Sakusa when they finally made it to their house in Kobe.

Sakusa nodded, impatiently.

“Ready.”

Chapter 12

“I can’t believe she pinched our phones,” Osamu murmured. “Rin is probably climbing the walls by now.”

“You still haven’t told me how he figured it out,” Atsumu complained. They were laying on the opposite ends of Osamu’s bed, braced on the pillows. Bored to death, they kept passing the ball to each other. The one who managed to whack the other in the face more times won.

“Someone sent him that stupid video of our fight,” Osamu admitted and grinned. “And then Rin called his parents and told them he really fucking tried but he’s as bent as a rainbow.”

Atsumu laughed out loud.

“He seriously said that?” he wanted to know.

“More or less. It turned out that he’s told them about his sexual orientation. They were not happy and enrolled him there with all the Omegas in hopes he would find at least one attractive. And he found. Me. He told me that it explained a lot since I was the first and only “Omega” that’s caught his attention.”

That actually made a lot of sense.

“That’s why he didn’t care you were such a prude! He was just happy that his parents were right and he could still push into the right hole!” Atsumu made quotation marks with his fingers. Osamu used the time to smack him in the face with the ball. “Au, Samu, you asshole!” The Omega kicked his brother in the shin and threw the ball back. Osamu dug in time, laughing in Atsumu’s face.
