Atsumu threw the ball at Osamu. Lucky as always, he managed to cover his face with both arms and the ball hit his elbow, bumped the cup with stationary and knocked it to the ground before landing next to the window. Osamu sighed and stood up to pick the ball.

Atsumu felt a pang of anxiety, seeing his brother’s surprised face. He approached the window and looked out, not sure what to expect. The worst, probably, whatever it was supposed to be. His parents moved the border of ‘the worst’ every single day, constantly finding things that Atsumu had found ‘the worst’ in the past more bearable than their newest stunts.

But, instead of the apocalypse itself unfolding in their front yard, a very familiar head of dark curls emerged from the car. Atsumu’s heart jumped in his chest.

“Omi!”

“What is he doing here?” Osamu asked, but Atsumu wasn’t listening anymore. Barefoot, he raced to the door and in seconds appeared in front of the house.

“What? I don’t deserve a hug?” the man asked, raising his eyebrows. “I brought him here from Tokyo.”

Atsumu gave him a hug as well, on a cloud nine.

“Thank you,” he told him happily.

“She had a coffee date wih one of her friends,” Osamu said, appearing outside. He nodded to Kiyoomi. “Hey, Sakusa. Take that idiot inside, he didn’t even put the shoes on before he jumped you like a rabid monkey.”

Osamu in Osaka and Atsumu in Tokyo.”

If they kick you out for good, we will find an alternative solution. All the same, you can pursue your dream career path. On some conditions, of course,” he continued, ignoring his wife’s protests.

“Akari, let it go. I’d rather let them do it and make sure they’re safe.”

Judging by the frown on his face, Haruo was done with listening.

“You’ve just described Sakusa,” Osamu told him.

“He’s my perfect Alpha, then!” Atsumu answered back and stuck his tongue out.

“See? Nothing there about money. Don’t choose someone who you would want. He’s already chosen. If it doesn’t work out for them, fine, life, he can find someone else. But at the end of the day, it has to be his choice.”

“And you’re just going to ignore the fact this… Alpha got Atsu into bed?”

“It was actually the other way around,” Osamu told her.

Kiyoomi blushed, feeling very uncomfortable with how he suddenly found himself in the middle of a huge family fight.

“Yeah, that. But still, I’d like to remind you that Atsumu proved to be more mature than we were his age. He went to a doctor and started taking birth control before he did anything sexual. It meant it was his conscious choice to let Sakusa touch him and he had full right to do so. You can dislike Sakusa-kun but it’s Atsumu that needs to like him in the end.”

“And that’s your final word? You’re not going to listen to anything I say?”

“I’m sorry, honey. I can’t support you in this. It’s time they start living their lives as adults.”

Silence fell. Akari looked around, taking in their reactions. Then, she swallowed hard and left the kitchen. Nobody followed her.

Haruo rubbed his face tiredly and sighed.

“So… I can really play?” Atsumu asked, unsure.

“Yes. You have my permission.”

“And Samu can cook?”

“Mhm.”

“Fuck yeah!”

The twins jumped into each other’s arms, too excited to sit still. Atsumu almost cried from overwhelming relief. He had been fighting so long and hard for it that it seemed like a dream.

“It doesn’t mean I’m not disappointed. I understand why you behaved the way you behaved and respect the effort, but I won’t simply forget. Osamu, I expect you to continue working and supporting yourself financially, at least till the end of this academic year. We can discuss the details later. I also want to meet your boyfriend. Atsumu’s case is more complicated if he gets the green light from the rector.”

“How… how do you know? Did you talk to somebody?”

“Yes, to the rector. Your coach helped a lot and took your side. Where do you think I took your boyfriend from? Found him in the park?”

Atsumu shrugged. He hadn’t thought about it, too excited to see him in person.

In the late evening, they were joined by Suna. Osamu called him the first minute he got his phone back. Suna was super pissed at first for being ghosted, but after a while, he relented and decided to let it go. He was in Osaka anyway, so reaching Kobe didn’t take him that long.

Waiting for Haruo to cook them late dinner, they decided to kill the time in the garden and play some football. Suna turned out to be an amazing and irritating defender and gave Atsumu and Kiyoomi a run for their money. Apart from Akari, they all were in a great mood.

From the moment she left the kitchen, she didn’t try to join them. She sat through dinner in silence, ignoring Haruo’s attempts at including her in the conversation. She had to see how happy the twins were, finally able to speak their mind freely, and how all the boys interacted with each other like a group of long-term friends. She didn’t even crack a smile at some stories Atsumu and Osamu had to tell that were very hush hush before. Only Kiyoomi was in the know since he had guessed Atsumu’s secondary gender at the very beginning. For Suna and the twins’ parents everything was kind of new.

When it was time to go to sleep, they faced the problem of where their guests should sleep. At first Haruo thought of separating Suna and Sakusa and letting them sleep in the living room, but then decided against it. They put an air mattress in the room. It wasn’t like there was going to be any hanky panky with the four of them in one room.

Atsumu fell asleep with a smile on his face after hours of hushed whispers and laughs they all shared in the darkness of his childhood room.

The next day he was woken up by an insistent hand yanking him by the T-shirt.

“Get up,” the Alpha murmured, basically rolling Atsumu’s stiff body from side to side. “The breakfast is ready.”

“Five more minutes.”

“No, no more minutes. Osamu said he’ll eat it himself if you don’t move your ass.”

Atsumu opened one eye and looked at Kiyoomi. He pulled him by the back of his neck and tried to make him lay down so they could snuggle under the cover. But, no matter how good he smelled and how much he tried, Kiyoomi didn’t budge. He huffed and ripped the cover off Atsumu’s body.

“What the… Omi!”

“It’s ten already. Get up.”

Atsumu moaned unhappily, but got up. Not like he had much of a choice. Pouting, he changed into comfortable tracksuit and they went to the kitchen. Just as Kiyoomi promised, the breakfast was ready and waiting on the table. They were alone with Suna and Kiyoomi, their parents both at work.

The afternoon was spent on long walks around the neighbourhood and showing their boyfriends their favourite places from childhood, trying to outdo each other in telling silly stories about the other one. After a few hours, Suna and Kiyoomi decided they knew more about them that they probably should at the stage of their relationships.

They also both agreed they were happy not to have a twin.

And it was all cool and awesome, and Atsumu would be extremely happy with how the day was going if it weren’t for one thing.

His mum.

And no, he didn’t forget about everything she had done to stop him from chasing his dreams. To force him into an undistinguished mold, ignoring his pleases and feelings. He remembered it well and knew he wouldn’t be able to forgive her any time soon. But it was the same person who had given birth to him and raised him to be a strong-minded, confident individual. She was the one taking care of his needs, came to his soccer games and school shows, baked delicious birthday cakes.

He didn’t want to lose all that only because they had different opinions about what his career should be like. Atsumu was greedy. Why would he give something up if there was a chance to have everything?

Kiyoomi was at his side and wasn’t going anywhere. His dad promised he could play, Osamu was doing great too. The only thing missing was his mum.

It was at the back of his mind and when a few hours later he noticed his mum sitting alone in the garden on his way to the kitchen, he stopped in his tracks, undecided. The door was ajar, and he could hear her soft sobs. He couldn’t just leave even if he wanted. Not when it was his mum.

With a mug of hot tea, he exited the house and went to talk to her, hoping they could get past their differences.

The moment Akari saw him, she tensed and turned her head to the side, trying to hide her tears. She wiped them quickly, but he knew she had cried.

“Atsumu. Do you need anything?” she asked him, still not looking him in the eyes.

“I’m coming in peace,” he told her jokingly, trying to loosen the mood. “I thought we should talk.”

She took the mug from him. They sat in silence for a few minutes, gathering their thoughts.

“I don’t want us to be like that,” Atsumu spoke up when it became apparent she wasn’t going to go first. “But I won’t quit soccer. Or Omi. I want you to be happy for me and support my choices.”

“You’re as stubborn as a mule,” she murmured in answer. “You’re not going to give me an inch, huh, Atsumu?” She rubbed her tired face and sighed. “And of course you inherited that pig-headed personality from me. I really have your best interest in mind.”

“I know. We both know that but you can’t decide everything for us. If one day an injury knocks me out of being a pro or I simply don’t make it into a pro team, then at least I will know I’ve done everything I could. I don’t want to regret anything. You can understand that, right?”

Akari chuckled, unable to hide her bitterness.

“That’s funny. A few months ago this conversation looked differently. I won’t point who stomped his feet and screamed in rage to get his way.” Atsumu shrugged. He hadn’t had a chance to change his parents’ decision then. But, he gained some experience over the months spent in Tokyo, and became more confident in his choices. And besides, his dad already told him that he could pursue soccer. There was no need to throw a temper tantrum. He’d already got what he wanted. “I won’t change my mind about it, Atsumu. Soccer is an unstable career, and for an Omega especially. There will be a moment when you will have to make a choice between soccer and family.”

“That’s my concern. I just want you to support us. And if it doesn’t work out, you can be the first person to scream at us that you told us so. And blame it all on Dad.”

“He totally deserves that. Prick. I just wanted to save you some pain and worries which we had to got through. He takes it as a rejection from me as if I didn’t want to be with him… And sure, life pushed us into each other’s arms sooner than we were ready, sooner than I could make a conscious decision… I won’t say I didn’t have moments of doubt, especially at the beginning, when you and Osamu were giving us a hard time. But from the time’s perspective, I can see that your dad is the best that could have happened to me. I doesn’t change the fact we had it hard, Atsumu. Very hard. Sometimes I wonder how we have made it at all. I don’t think we would have survived if it wasn’t for you keeping us focused on what was important. But it was a hard life lesson, one I wish you could be spared.”

“I don’t care about money.”

Akari snorted. “Don’t be naive, Atsumu. You were in Tokyo. You had to make a living somehow. You should understand how lack of money complicates life.”

Atsumu hummed, thinking about it for a moment.

“Sure, it wasn’t easy. But I learnt how to deal with it and how to make ends meet. And I still believe money isn’t that important. I’d be happy if you give Omi a chance.”

Akari scratched her ear. “Are you serious, Atsumu? I won’t say I don’t see the appeal, but it’s the most eccentric kid I have ever seen in my life. He can’t be that good in bed.”

Atsumu snorted, blushing. “Trust me, it’s not that. He’s a weirdo, but I love him for that. He’s very… perceptive and intelligent. Brutally honest and ridiculously gifted. He knew I was an Omega from the very beginning, but he kept it in secret. He can take all the credit for my good grades because he’s so anal about his stupid rule that responsibilities first, pleasure later. And he’s treating me well.”

“I’m not thrilled that you have sex with him but,” she sighed, “I was your age and I know how it is. I don’t like it. At all, but your dad already decided, huh? Not like I can stop any of you. So, alright. I will give him a chance and I will try to accept your decisions, but I hope your little shits will give you as much of a hard time as you and Osamu have been giving us.” She smirked at him.

“Thanks a lot, mum,” he murmured, pretending to be irritated, but he quickly stopped and grinned at her. Akari’s lower lip wobbled and she pulled him into her arms.

“I’m proud of you, Atsumu. Even if you may sometimes feel I’m not.”

The rest of the conversation went the way it used to for them. Good-naturedly, with lots of teasing remarks and jokes. He opened up about the swap, how he got interested in Kiyoomi, how many friends he’d made. Akari seemed relieved hearing that. He had never mentioned anybody whenever he came to visit, and she admitted they were worried about him. And well, they couldn’t contain their happiness that it wasn’t actually him trying to be a professional cook, knowing how much he sucked in the kitchen.

Much, much later they joined othersin the living room and played board games. Akari even asked Sunarin and Kiyoomi some questions. They both gladly answered, understanding how important it was for the Miya family.

Atsumu and Osamu shared a look, their eyes shining with excitement. It meant everything to them.

A few days later, the dreadful day arrived. The university was about to decide what to do with Atsumu.

They sat in the living room and spent hours in silence, waiting impatiently.

When Haruo’s phone rang, Atsumu jumped to his feet. His heart was beating so fast he could feel it in his throat. His chewed his nails to the point of drawing blood to Kiyoomi’s disgust. He couldn’t help it, though. The stress was making him almost levitate, and his nervousness seemed to be contagious, because everybody seemed on edge. Well, apart from Suna, who was cool as a cucumber and focused on scrolling his Instagram.

The conversation lasted for less than a minute, and Haruo’s face told Atsumu everything he needed to know.

He shook his head. “Seventy percent voted against. They won’t let you go back. They believe you made too big of a mess. You are free to enroll next year if you want, but you won’t be permitted to join the soccer team.”

Atsumu swallowed hard, his lower lip wobbling and stomach dropping. He could not believe his ears. He was so close. So close! So many people had his back and the university still…

It was all for nothing.

“We’ll figure something else out,” Haruo told him, trying to lift his spirit, but Atsumu shook his head.

“I want to be alone,” he said quietly and left the room, feeling his eyes brimming with tears. He put his shoes on and exited the house in need of fresh air to clear his thoughts.

He barely made it onto the main street when Kiyoomi caught up with him, worried by his behavior. Atsumu opened his mouth to chase him away, but ultimately decided to leave him be. In silence, they arrived at the playground and sat down on the swings in the shadows where Osamu and Atsumu had spent a lot of time as little kids. Kiyoomi didn’t say anything, letting him gather his thoughts and cry in peace. Atsumu reached out to him, seeking some comfort.

“It’s so fucking unfair,” he finally uttered, feeling totally dejected and crestfallen.

“I know. But your dad is right. There are other places that would be more than happy to have you.”

“Are you absolutely certain, Omi? Because it feels like obstacle after obstacle here. Nobody treats me seriously because I’m a damn Omega.”

“I’m absolutely sure.” Kiyoomi crouched in front of him and cupped his face, looking him in the eyes. His expression was serious. “You knew from the beginning that it wouldn't be easy. You swapped with Osamu to play and by doing that, you omitted the problem, but you had to know that it won’t actually solve it. That some people will stand in your way. Am I right?”

Atsumu nodded, yet he didn’t understand what Kiyoomi was trying to say.

“So nothing changed,” the Alpha continued. “You shouldn’t be surprised they rejected you. There will be many people in your way and they will do the exact same thing. And fuck them all with a chainsaw.” Atsumu twitched, surprised by the sudden curse and the vivid image it painted for him. “You don’t need them to get through. You already managed to convince your parents to give you a chance. You may not be able to be in our team, but it won’t erase the matches you’ve already played. So instead of focusing on them making your life hard, focus on how to solve this fucking problem.”

Atsumu sobbed, taken aback.

“Wow, Omi… If you don’t make it in soccer, you should go into coaching. You sure know how to pick your words.”

“If you were raised in my family, you’d know too. I told you that convincing my parents required a nimble mind of an ancient philosopher and Herkulean muscles.”

Atsumu laughed, wiping his tears.

“Well, we can agree on one thing. I should have expected this outcome. I was too spoiled with all the successes…” He sighed and stretched his arms out. “I bet on Tokyo because our parents wanted Osamu to study there. I have to become famous just to spite these assholes and set their asses on fire on social media.”

Kiyoomi smirked. “I’ll gladly help you. Seems like I have quite a lot of ammo in my arsenal.”

“Suna can help us make it go viral…”

“And Osamu will pretend he hates it but secretly create tons of fake profiles to help it gain more popularity.”

That completely amused Atsumu because it was so in Osamu’s style.

“Better?” Kiyoomi asked him softly, tilting his head to the side. 

Atsumu smiled and kissed him on the cheek. His eyes were still wet from tears, but shone with a new-found determination.

“Better. He laughs best who laughs last, huh? I’ll do whatever I can to be the one who gets the last laugh.”

“Let’s go back. I got so worried my stomach is all in knots. I need something herbal to soothe it before I hurl.”

Atsumu chuckled and nodded obediently. Kiyoomi pulled him up and hugged for a good measure before they made their way back home.

Fours pairs of worried eyes turned in their direction when they entered. Atsumu blinked at their expressions and smiled.

“I’m fine. And starving!”

“Are you okay?” Akari asked, not able to hide her confusion over Atsumu’s calm demeanor. Atsumu could be very volatile at times, and held a grudge forever.

“Yeah, I'm over it.”

Akari and Haruo shared a puzzled look before turning their eyes to Kiyoomi who only shrugged and sat at the table.

“Are you sure? You seemed… down.” 

“I’m not anymore. Omi put me back together in three sentences.”

“I hope it isn’t the beginning of a dirty joke?” Osamu vinced.

Atsumu rolled his eyes. “No. I simply won’t care about some idiots standing in my way. I didn’t when you had a lot to say about it,” he looked at his parents, “and I’m not going to care about them. Omi said that they are not first and certainly not last and he’s totally right. I should have expected that. It’s only one of the ways to get me where I want to be and I just need to explore other possibilities.”

Suna smiled, amused. “I like the way you’re thinking.”

The sudden change in Atsumu’s mood pleased everybody, although it was obviously unexpected. The way Kiyoomi manage to contain Atsumu’s temper was unusual and they all noticed. Atsumu had always been difficult and confrontational, yet the Alpha needed only an hour with him to talk him down. It was impressive.

Not only did Atsumu get his shit together in record time, he also started thinking about possible solutions right away. Before he had left to Tokyo, two soccer academies wanted him to join. They had to take some other people in, but it didn’t mean they wouldn’t want him for an upcoming season. Nobody was going to punch him for asking. He had a few months to plan his moves. He was ready to fight.

 

______________________

 

It was a beautiful Saturday morning two weeks later. Atsumu came back from his ten kilometer run and realized in the genkan that his dad had guests. He peeked into the living room, curious.

Suna and Osamu had left for their university in Osaka, and Kiyoomi was long gone in Tokyo. That couldn’t be them.

“Atsumu! Finally!” Haruo smiled and ushered him inside.

Atsumu looked down. He didn’t look best. His T-shirt was soaked with sweat and his face was definitely red from exertion. He still entered, not wanting to be rude since the guests already knew he was there.

He frowned. He could swear one of them seemed familiar, but Atsumu couldn’t place him.

“Gentlemen, this is my son, Miya Atsumu.” Atsumu bowed politely, puzzled. If it was another attempt at matchmaking, he was going to blow up. “Atsumu, this is Haruno Daiki and Samson Foster. The owner and main coach of MSBY Black Jackals.”

Atsumu froze. That’s why the old man’s face had seemed familiar! The sports news had a lot to say about his transfer from the first league in France to Japan.

“Uhm, hi?”

Haruno snorted with laughter. “Hi,” he replied, grinning. He was young. Thirty, maybe thirty-something. Hard to believe he owned a club such as MSBY, but well, Atsumu had no idea who owned it. Only who coached and played there. “Sit down. We have a proposition for you, one we hope you won’t decline.”

Atsumu obediently sat down, palms suddenly sweaty and heart beating fast in his chest. Were they about to do what he thought they were about to do?

“Let’s not keep him dangling,” the coach murmured, seeing his shaking hands. “Atsumu-kun, we’ve seen some of your matches this season. We were very impressed with your skills. We hoped you could be interested in signing with us.”

“You want me?” he asked, voice high in disbelief. He had been waiting and dreaming about that moment but it felt too surreal to be true. “You know I’m an Omega?”

“That’s part of the reason why we want you,” Haruno interjected. “You grabbed our attention but we didn’t plan on making you an offer this year. We’re trying to strengthen our offense, but in a few years, we thought, you would make a good addition to our team. The mess with your status made us reconsider. You see, I’m an Omega myself. I inherited the club after the death of my mate. Not many people are aware of the situation. It pissed me off how twisted everybody’s attitute towards Omegas is, especially in sport. Having an Omega in the team isn’t prohibited anymore but still, not many teams decide to offer them contracts. I promised myself to change that with some promising Omegas in my team since I’m the one who can decide that. To stir the pot, so to say, and prompt others to do the same. I want to start with you. You’re good, but you can be better. And if you agree, Coach Foster will make a real pro out of you.”

“Where is the catch?” Atsumu asked. “It sounds too good to be true.”

Haruno smirked. “Because you’re used to being denied anywhere you go. I know what’s it like. You showed balls with that twin swap. Coach Foster agrees you’ve got potential. He is interested in that potential. Me? These balls. The contract I want to offer you is a standard one we offer all rookies. The only difference is that you need to be under doctor’s supervision and take injections with suppressants regularly to ensure your safety. I want to prove we can compete with Alphas and Betas just fine, thank you very much.”

Atsumu took a long contract from the man. It had many pages, the font was small. It was real. He looked at his dad, astonished, but the answer could be only one.

“You know I’ll agree. I would be stupid if I didn’t,” he admitted.

“But first,” his dad stopped him in his tracks, “we need some time to consult the conditions with our lawyer to make sure it’s okay.”

“Of course,” the owner agreed without batting an eye. “Like I said, it’s a standard contract we draw for all rookies with some added rules for safety of all players. We don’t want Atsumu to be blamed for being provocative or something along these lines. Playing with Alphas means sharing common spaces with them, along with hotel and locker rooms, showers. You didn't have a problem with that, but I guess being incognito helped you feel more comfortable. This time everybody will know you’re an Omega.”

“It shouldn’t be a problem,” Atsumu told them after a short moment of consideration. “Until high school, I shared all these spaces with my teammates. Omegas are discriminated against in pro leagues, that’s it. Which proves how stupid it all is. I even shared a room in our dorm with an Alpha.”

They nodded, happy with that answer. They asked if Atsumu had any questions, but he was completely taken aback with them showing up out of nowhere, so he couldn’t think of many. His dad, though, he wanted to know a lot, and it took them almost two more hours to satisfy his doubts and curiosity.

Then, Foster and Haruno left, leaving them alone in the house and stunned.

“I’ll get it to a lawyer today. We need to know what he will say.”

“I will agree anyway. Even if the conditions are poor. I need it.”

“Atsumu…”

“It’s a first league team, Dad! In Osaka where Samu is! A chance like that may not appear again!”

“I understand, but I don’t want you to get your hopes up. We need to make sure this contract is worth your time.”

“It’s my chance!”

Haruo smiled, shaking his head. “Stubborn like always.” He kissed him on the forehead. “Alright. But I’m still going. You don’t feel bad for your Alpha?”

Atsumu frowned. “Omi? Why?”

“I heard you were discussing renting a flat together in Tokyo…”

Atsumu scratched the back of his head. True, he and Kiyoomi had that idea before the Alpha had taken a train back to Tokyo. Breaking up was out of the question despite the distance. So renting something together seemed like a good option since Atsumu didn’t have to be anywhere specific for a few months.

MSBY Black Jackals was a team from Osaka. Playing for them meant Atsumu wouldn’t be able to be in Tokyo much.

Still… He didn’t think Kiyoomi would have a problem with that. The Alpha understood how big of a chance it was, especially for Atsumu. For the first time ever his secondary orientation was about to push him forward, not hinder him.

Kiyoomi would never stand in his way. Ever.

“We’ll manage,” he assured his dad. Seeing his skeptical expression, he rolled his eyes. “You will see. Omi wants to go pro, too. He would have already it it wasn’t for his parents. We will figure it out.”

“If you say so.”

Haruo didn’t seem convinced, but he dropped the topic.

“Speaking of Omi, I better call him and share the good news!”

Kiyoomi pretended to be surprised but he was a shitty liar and Atsumu saw right through him.

“Omi, you knew?!” he asked him with disbelief.

Kiyoomi sighed. “I was passing by when they were waiting in front of the coach’s office to discuss Bokuto. They were gossiping about our team. Coach Foster mentioned they need your address so I gave it to them,” he admitted, embarrassed.

Atsumu gawked, his mouth open.

“You butted in on their conversation?!”

“They weren’t very subtle,” he tried to defend himself.

Atsumu’s heart swelled with love.

“I would kiss and cuddle you to death but I’m too far.” He noticed Bokuto behind Kiyoomi’s shoulder. He grinned. “Bokkun! Hey!”

“Tsum-Tsum!” Bokuto smiled widely, seeing him on the screen. “When are you coming?!”

“I’ll visit soon, I promise. Do me a favor and hug and kiss Omi for me. I won’t be able to sleep if someone doesn’t do it in my stead!”

Bokuto didn’t need to be told twice. “Okay!”

The phone was shoved into somebody else’s hand and Bokuto literally jumped on spluttering Kiyoomi, engulfing him in a bear hug. Atsumu cackled, hearing the wild protests. Akaashi’s face appeared on the screen.

“Hey! It’s good to see you. What’s up?”

“You, too,” Akaashi answered, unbothered by the ruckus the two Alphas were making behind his back. “Kiyoomi told me. Congratulations, Atsumu!”

“Thanks! I still can’t believe it. Omi admitted he helped me a little.”

“A little?” Akaashi was clearly amused. “With a poker face, he told them you’re the best playmaker he had ever played with, and that these academic pigs lost their minds with what they did to you. Then Bokuto-san appeared, heard the entire thing and joined him, telling them how much their butt is going to get kicked since you’re no longer here and Oikawa is abroad. The captain of MSBY eventually snapped and told him that if everything goes according to plan, Bokuto will enjoy your company at Jackal’s training.”

“Wow, seriously?!” Atsumu felt tears in his eyes at that heart-warming display of loyalty. He didn’t expect them to be so intense. “Bokuto, one more time, please!” Kiyoomi, face red as a tomato, shot Bokuto a glare, but Bokuto didn’t care and hesitated only for a second. Then he attacked himagain, grinning like a child. “Akaashi, you gotta give him the best blowjob ever in thanks for me. I’m begging you.”

Akaashi snorted. “That can be arranged.”

“Tsum-Tsum! Does it mean we’re going to play for the Jackals together?!” Bokuto exclaimed loudly, bracing his chin on Akaashi’s shoulder.

“Have you signed already?” Atsumu asked curiously. Bokuto nodded. “Awesome! My dad wants to run it through a lawyer to make sure it’s okay.”

“I can send you mine if you want? You can compare them.”

Atsumu hesitated. “Is it okay?”

“No,” Akaashi told him. “But who cares? Nobody needs to know. You won’t have a better chance to make sure.”

Atsumu didn’t want to get Bokuto in trouble but Akaashi was right. It could stay between them and he wouldn’t have a better chance to check if Haruno’s words were sincere.

“I’d be very grateful, Bokkun.”

“I’ll send you everything later today,” the Alpha promised cheerfully.

Atsumu breathed a sigh of relief. He wanted to play for the MSBY. He was afraid that he wouldn’t get another chance like that. On the other hand, it was a contract that could mess up his life big time if he wasn’t careful.

“Let me talk to Atsumu,” Kiyoomi told them from somewhere in the background. Akaashi shrugged and passed the phone. Atsumu laughed seeing his messy curls and red cheeks. It was obvious the Alpha had tried to smoothe it, but it was a fool’s errand.

“Omi, stop scowling. Somebody had to cuddle you since I’m not there to do it.”

“You’re gonna pay for it. You and Bokuto,” he threatened. “And congrats, Atsu. You worked hard for that contract.”

“Thanks, Omi,” Atsumu replied softly, suddenly feeling emotional. “I wouldn’t make it so far without your help, and the guys… I hope one day I can make it into the first string… And that, one day, you will be on the same pitch.”

Kiyoomi only nodded, his face serious.

“Of course. But not just yet. We can discuss it in detail when you visit, alright? I don’t want to talk about it on the phone.”

“Sure.”

They talked a little bit more about everything and nothing, the mood easy-going and relaxed. Kiyoomi told him that his family had become insufferable, trying to get some info about Atsumu out of him. He also uncertainly asked if Atsumu wanted to meet them. Of course, Atsumu accepted even if the idea of meeting Kiyoomi’s family scared him. He was not the one to back out of a challenge, though, and that was not different.

When they ended the call, Atsumu suddenly realized that for the first time ever, Osamu wasn’t the first person on his mind to share something important with. It was a weird feeling, since Osamu was always the one to get the news ASAP. Maybe because they were inseparable or maybe because Atsumu simply trusted him that much with his secrets.

It felt weird to do it differently and confide in Kiyoomi instead of Osamu.

But damn, it felt good.

 

Chapter End Notes

Surprise, surprise! I'm here! And it's not even an April Fool's joke!
After checking the draft, I decided to combine the last two chapters, so there is only one more left! The reason for that is the length - there is no point in splitting the content since there isn't that much left of the story.
Which is a huge freaking relief. I realized a few weeks ago that I started posting this story in 2021 and my soul literally left my body for a moment. I want to get it done as soon as possible because it's long overdue. Initially, I was thinking about prolonging it, making Atsumu go back to university, room with Akaashi (who doesn't have a roommate since Iwaizumi left with Oikawa), but I wasn't sure what then, so I think this way we have a pretty solid wrap up.
Let me know what you think about this chapter and kudo if you like it! See you soon for the final one, hopefully sooner rather than later :)
And a huge <3 for everybody who commented on the last chapter. You're part of the reason this one is finished so quickly.

Chapter 13

Chapter Notes

Yo!
FINALLY! For those who like sappy and traditional endings, after a long deliberation I decided to include an epilog because I was well programmed over the years to consider it 'having everything'. If you prefer to left it more open, skip the epilog part :) It's up to you how you imagine the future for them as long as it's HAPPY!
Enjoy!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Atsumu’s brain stopped at the ‘I love you’ part and disregarded the rest completely. His heart started to beat fast.

EPILOG

 

[And it’s started! The first V. League match between MSBY Black Jackals and Schweiden Adlers! I have to admit I’ve been waiting for it for months!]

[And you weren’t the only one, Minori. Both teams proved they can surprise. Both are hungry for the win this season and both acquired new, promising players who are debuting today.]

[True, true. One of them is Hinata Shouyou who spent the past two years in Argentina, learning from the best street soccer players in the world. We don’t have much information about him, but we managed to establish that he actually played in high school with Kageyama Tobio who is the key player for the Adlers.]

[Whoa, seriously?!]

[Seriously! A lot of talented players here are close in age, so they probably know one another quite well.]

[{laugh} I have to say I’m relieved. Fans weren’t happy when Sakusa joined the MSBY a few months ago even though he had been the university’s top scorer and MVP.]

[Took out sounds terrible, Minori. For people unaware of the situation, Miya Atsumu and Sakusa Kiyoomi are mates. Rumor has it that they started dating as freshmen at university. Last year Miya announced on his Instagram that they were expecting and he wouldn’t play for a while for the obvious reason. Fans were crushed. Miya didn’t play in the semi-finals and many people think his absence is what caused the team to lose. Sakusa was branded ‘guilty’ on that front and took a huge blow before he even signed with the team.]

The MSBY Black Jackals won the first match three to one. Atsumu played for about an hour, still not back to his usual condition. One of the sports reporters asked for a quick interview and Atsumu answered his questions easily. He had gotten used to being known and bothered, and since the times when he blurted something he shouldn’t have were mostly over, talking in front of the camera wasn’t so stressful anymore. “Would you like to tell us something about your pup?”

“Oi, he isn’t that bad, don’t exaggerate.”

“For you because I’m the one who takes care of him at night.”

Atsumu smiled. It was the truth. Kiyoomi had a sixth sense when it came to Kiyoshi. The moment the pup woke up and started wiggling and sobbing, Kiyoomi was already there, looking for the source of discomfort. Atsumu had no idea how he was doing this and it irritated him that his Alpha beat him to it every single time.

When Kiyoshi finished his bottle, they collected their things and went back home. Osamu was waiting there for them. He promised to babysit his nephew for a few hours and let Atsumu and Kiyoomi rest after the match. The beginning of the season was never easy, so his support—and the delicious food he had brought from his restaurant—were greatly appreciated. The restaurant was a hit, partially thanks to Atsumu who advertised it on his social media and brought new people in. And when someone came and tried the food, many of them simply wanted to come back for more. Akaashi alone could probably keep the restaurant afloat, considering how often and how much he ate there.

Enjoying the peace and quiet for a moment, they climbed into their bed and decided to take a nap. They didn’t have much time just for them. Just to be and not worry about everything and anything.

Kiyoomi spooned him from behind and rubbed his nose over the bite mark on his neck. Atsumu smiled softly. He was sore and needed a long massage but he was getting into shape much quicker than anticipated. People were surprised but he wasn’t. For Atsumu, mindset was everything. People and things can hold you back only if you let them. So honestly, people were their own enemies. They held themselves back. The moment Atsumu decided to just go there and take it all, the world became his.

“Love you,” Kiyoomi murmured into his neck sleepily.

“Love you, too,” Atsumu answered softly, content.

 

THE END

End Notes

Hi!
I know some of you are waiting for the next part of the tribes and I promise I'm working on it! But... I really wanted to publish something and this story is almost finished anyway, so I think it's safe to share it with you.
It's really silly and very self-indulgent, but I was really into it and the new chapters just popped out of nowhere. In this one, they play soccer because I was inspired by the movie 'She's the man' and I decided to stick with the concept.
The story should have around 15 chapters in total (I have almost 12 written in Polish, so it's easier to write it in English when I have a point of reference xd). It's a little bumpy but should be more smooth from the time on.
The title should be read as 'Don't hold me back' or 'Hold me'.
I hope you like it. All mistakes are mine.
